1801 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Haggerty v. County of Kings


Civ. No. 4380


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


117 Cal. App. 2d 470; 256 P.2d 393; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1838; 32 L.R.R.M. 2185; 23 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,611



April 28, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County. Stanley Murray, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to restrain interference with peaceful picketing and enforcement of county ordinances relating to parades and use of loud speakers on public highways.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment for defendants on sustaining demurrer to complaint without leave to amend reversed as to cause of action involving constitutionality of ordinance relating to parades on public highway; affirmed as to other cause of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the secretary of a labor federation (secretary), appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County (California) that was entered against it in its action that sought to restrain defendants, county and county officials, from interfering with the labor federation's peaceful picketing and from enforcing certain county ordinances relating to parades and use of loud speakers on public highways.


OVERVIEW: The secretary filed an action against defendants in his individual capacity and on behalf of the labor federation. The action sought to obtain an injunction against the county officers that would restrain them from interfering with peaceful picketing and the enforcement of two ordinances. One ordinance dictated controls for parades and processions on public highways in the county (parade ordinance), and the other ordinance set forth guidelines for the use of loud speakers in public (speaker ordinance). The trial court sustained defendants' demurrer to the complaint and entered judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court reversed that portion of the trial court judgment that sustained defendants' demurrer to the action against the parade ordinance. Its holding rested on the conclusion that an ordinance that vested arbitrary discretion in a county officer for issuance of parade permits presented an unconstitutional restraint on the picketers' free speech rights. However, the court affirmed that portion of the of the trial court's judgment that upheld the speaker ordinance, as it was a constitutional limitation on speech rights of the picketers.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that was entered in favor of defendants and that sustained their demurrer to the complaint was reversed as to the secretary' constitutional challenge to the county ordinance relating to parades on public highways. However, the trial court's judgment entered in favor of defendants was affirmed as the ordinance that governed the use of loud speakers in public venues.

 

1802 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Markus v. Justice's Court of Little Lake Township


Civ. No. 8282


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


117 Cal. App. 2d 391; 255 P.2d 883; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1825



April 21, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Mendocino County. Lilburn Gibson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus and in prohibition to restrain a justice's court from further proceedings in a prosecution for violation of an ordinance regarding the keeping and control of dogs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dog owner sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Mendocino County (California) that denied his petition for writs of mandamus and prohibition to require appellee governmental unit to refrain from further prosecution of the dog owner for violation of the governmental unit's ordinance regarding the keeping and control of dogs.


OVERVIEW: The dog owner argued that the governmental unit's ordinance was void because it placed unreasonable restrictions on the ownership and possession of dogs in rural and sparsely inhabited areas. He also contended that the ordinance did not contain a definite or ascertainable meaning for the word "premises." Finally, the governmental unit's ordinance attempted to legislate in a field completely occupied by state statute. The court rejected all of the dog owner's arguments and affirmed the trial court's decision to deny the writs. The court pointed out that once the legislature had spoken, the question for the court was not the propriety of the legislation but rather the power to legislate. The court then noted that the law was well settled that the legislative bodies had the right to impose restrictions on the rights of dog owners. The court also noted that the word "premises" was clear and certain and not vague so as to render the ordinance unconstitutional. Finally, the ordinance at issue here was not precluded due to being preempted by state statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that denied the dog owner's petition for writs of mandamus and prohibition.

 

1803 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 19234


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


116 Cal. App. 2d 856; 254 P.2d 935; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1152



March 24, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 9, 1953, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 21, 1953. Gibson, C. J., and Spence, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Dudley G. McGregor, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for an injunction and for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted plaintiff landowners' prayer to declare Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code §§ 12.11-C, 4, 12.21-C, 1(j), and 12.21-C, 1(k), unconstitutional as to them and to enjoin the city from prosecuting or bringing any action based on the ordinances against them.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances provided that every lot in a multiple dwelling zone had to have a minimum width and area, and that no lot held under separate ownership at the time of the ordinances' adoption could be separated or reduced below the minimums. After adoption, the landowners purchased the disputed lot and sold part of it so that neither resulting lot met the width requirements. The landowners were then criminally prosecuted for failing to comply with the municipal code. The court found that the ordinances were invalid as applied to the landowners' sale of part of the lot and to their ownership of the remainder because they did nothing out of conformity with the general conditions in the neighborhood. For at least 75 years, the neighborhood had been permitted to develop without interference by the city and enforcing the ordinances against such property did not accomplish any legislative purpose. The landowners and the buyer had all the usual residential facilities and their occupancy as separate owners did not interfere with the health, safety, or welfare of the community. The court affirmed the judgment that granted the landowners' prayer for injunctive and declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that declared certain ordinances invalid as to the landowners and that restrained the city from prosecuting or bringing any civil or criminal action based on the ordinances against them.

 

1804 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bldg. Maint. Contractors Ass'n


No. 14,868


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


253 P.2d 983; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 2053



March 3, 1953, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed from an order of a trial court (California), which first awarded it judgment in its suit against defendants, a maintenance contractors association and its members, for violations of the Cartwright Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 16,700 through 16,758, but which then granted the association and its members a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The association supplied 90 percent of the janitorial services in San Francisco, California, that were contracted out. The association only allowed competitive bidding on jobs under certain circumstances. The State alleged violations of the Cartwright Act for restraint of trade. The trial court enjoined the association from continuing its alleged conspiracy, but then instead granted a new trial. The court reversed on appeal, finding that the original injunction was correct. The court found that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 16,723 and 16,725 were both unconstitutionally vague in that they created exceptions for "reasonable profits" and the "furtherance of trade" that could not be defined with precision. Thus, both statutes were struck down. The only "trade" being "furthered" was that of the members themselves. Both statutes were severable from the Cartwright Act, leaving the original judgment against the association and its members intact. The association was a "trust" in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 16,720.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order for a new trial, leaving the original injunction against the association and its members intact.

 

1805 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reimringer


Crim. No. 2843


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


116 Cal. App. 2d 332; 253 P.2d 756; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1075



February 27, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant Raegan's Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 14, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County. Hugh Donovan, Judge.

Prosecution for abortion and conspiracy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of conviction affirmed as to defendant Raegan on all counts; affirmed as to defendant Reimringer on some counts and reversed on others.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which found defendants guilty by a jury on four counts of abortion and one count of conspiracy in a case brought by the State of California.


OVERVIEW: Police officers recognized suspicious circumstances at defendants' house. Upon questioning and following one of the defendants, who was a doctor, back into the house the officers found an aborted girl and instruments of the abortion. Defendant urged that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the verdict and judgment. The court held that a showing of another offense, similar in all respects, committed by the same defendant, and based on the same plan was good corroboration. The proven abortion of the first count was legally sufficient to corroborate the similar abortions in the other counts. As to the evidence of the doctor defendant, all the elements of participation in the crimes were shown. It was shown that he got the abortees, furnished his kitchen for the operations, and aided his codefendant in performing the operations. As to the codefendant, the evidence plainly supported the conviction on the first and fifth counts of abortion. The evidence was less satisfactory as to the other accounts. The judgment against defendant was affirmed in all five counts. The judgment against the codefendant on the first and fifth counts was affirmed. The remaining counts were reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment against defendant, which found him guilty of four counts of abortion and one count of conspiracy was affirmed. The judgment against the codefendant on the first and fifth counts was affirmed. As to the remaining counts, the judgment was reversed for a new trial.

 

1806 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Beery v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 19009


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


116 Cal. App. 2d 290; 253 P.2d 1005; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1069



February 26, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 23, 1953. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County dismissing action. Daniel N. Stevens, Judge.

Action to recover taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order dismissing action on sustaining demurrer to amended complaint and plaintiff's failure to amend within time allowed, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executors sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed their suit against respondents, tax assessor, tax collector, city, and county, challenging the assessment taxes against the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: Respondents levied various property taxes against the decedent's estate. After the executors challenged the tax assessment unsuccessfully before the county board of supervisors, they paid the taxes involuntarily and under protest. The executors then brought suit against respondents in the superior court. The superior court sustained a demurrer to the executors' complaint and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that federal reserve notes and bank notes in the estate were not exempt from taxation under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 212 because they were not encompassed in the meaning of the word "notes" as used in § 212. The court reasoned that the legislature intended the word "notes" to have included unconditional promises to pay an amount of money. Because federal reserve notes and bank notes were actual legal tender, the court determined that they were not intended to have been covered by § 212. The court also found that the federal reserve notes and bank notes were not solvent credits under § 113.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the executors' suit against respondents challenging the assessment of property taxes against the decedent's estate.

 

1807 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sica


Crim. No. 4942


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


116 Cal. App. 2d 59; 253 P.2d 75; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1039



February 13, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 12, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County denying petition to vacate a judgment. Charles W. Fricke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed on motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied defendant's petition to vacate a judgment. The petition to vacate the judgment was filed after defendant was convicted of conspiracy to violate Cal. Penal. Code § 337a.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of conspiracy to violate Cal. Penal Code § 337a, defendant appealed to the court. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. Thereafter, defendant filed his petition and notice of motion to vacate or set aside the judgment that was entered against him. After the trial court denied his motion, defendant appealed. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Penal Code § 1265. Section 1265 provided that if a judgment had been affirmed on appeal it was not proper to bring a coram nobis proceeding. According to defendant, the amendment to Cal Penal Code § 1265 was an unconstitutional legislative encroachment on the original jurisdiction of the trial court as provided in Cal. Const. art. VI8 § 5. The court held that the amendment to Cal. Penal Code § 1265 did not divest the trial court of any measure of jurisdiction conferred upon it by the California Constitution. Moreover, the court held that Cal. Penal Code § 1265 was procedural in character and therefore, within the constitutional power of the legislature. Lastly, the court found that there were no violations of defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

 

1808 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Shaw


Crim. No. 4955


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


115 Cal. App. 2d 753; 252 P.2d 970; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1733



February 3, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 5, 1953. Schauer, J., and Spence, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ in habeas corpus to secure her release from custody at a state hospital where she had been committed as an insane person by the Municipal Court of Los Angeles County (California).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with disturbing the peace. When her case came to trial, the municipal court had a doubt as to her sanity and ordered the criminal proceedings suspended. After a municipal court trial on defendant's sanity, defendant was found insane and was committed to the state hospital until she should regain her sanity. The court stated that the municipal court did not have jurisdiction to conduct a proceeding to determine the present sanity of a person whether the question arose in the course of a criminal cause or otherwise. Although the municipal court had jurisdiction of misdemeanors, a proceeding to determine the question of sanity of a defendant was not a part of a criminal trial. It was a special proceeding that was civil in character. When a doubt arose as to the sanity of defendant, it was not only the duty of the municipal court to order a trial of the issue and to suspend all proceedings in the criminal prosecution, but the trial court also had to certify the proceedings to the superior court. Therefore, the commitment of defendant to the state hospital was void and she was entitled to be released from the custody of that institution.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered that the state hospital release defendant from confinement therein.

 

1809 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Corona v. Corona Daily Independent


Civ. No. 4486


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


115 Cal. App. 2d 382; 252 P.2d 56; 1953 Cal. App. LEXIS 1671



January 15, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 6, 1953, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 12, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. R. Bruce Findlay, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to collect a business license tax.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for defendant reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Corona (city) sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) that found in favor of defendant newspaper in an action to collect a business license fee imposed on the newspaper.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court determined the question was: Did the city's ordinance, insofar as it levied a business tax per quarter upon the business of newspaper publications within the city abridge the freedom of the press in violation of the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution? The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the business tax was valid. The court found that a nondiscriminatory tax, levied upon the doing of business, for the sole purpose of maintaining the municipal government, without whose municipal services and protection the press could neither exist nor function, was to be sustained as being within the purview and necessary implications of the United States Constitution and its amendments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the newspaper was not exempt from the business license tax.

 

1810 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Forde v. Corte Madera


Civ. No. 15302


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


115 Cal. App. 2d 32; 251 P.2d 988; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1764



December 23, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 19, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County. Homer W. Patterson, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action in quo warranto to have set aside and declared invalid a proceeding for annexation of territory to a municipal corporation.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city and real property owners, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which denied their motion to set aside and declare invalid a proceeding for annexation of territory to defendant town.


OVERVIEW: The city and the real property owners filed an action in quo warranto to set aside and declare invalid the town's annexation of land that was owned by the real property owners. The trial court ruled in favor of the town. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Cal. Gov't Code §§ 35308, 35309 granted priority to the town as the annexor prior in time. The statutes constituted a positive prohibition of subsequent proceedings. Subsequent proceedings by the city to annex the property were an absolute nullity and were void. No life could be breathed into such void subsequent proceedings by the failure to contest them under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 349 1/2. Section 349 1/2 could not operate, as against a prior valid proceeding, to vitalize a completely invalid subsequent proceeding. A railroad right of way between the city and the town did not prevent physical contiguity of the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the town and against the city and the real property owners in their action to set aside and declare invalid a proceeding for annexation of territory to the town.

1812 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Denny v. Watson


Civ. No. 18990


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


114 Cal. App. 2d 491; 250 P.2d 692; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1197



December 2, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 22, 1953. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Frank G. Swain, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel Real Estate Commissioner to restore to them their licenses as real estate brokers.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment against petitioners affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate brokers sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which refused to grant them a writ of mandate to compel respondent Real Estate Commissioner to restore to them their license as real estate brokers.


OVERVIEW: The brokers challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 10177.5, 10176(i), 10177(f) (1945) on the ground that they violated due process of law guaranteed by the state and federal constitutions and that § 10177.5 denied them equal protection of the laws because it singled out real estate brokers. Under § 10177.5, the Commissioner had conducted a hearing and revoked the brokers' real estate licenses based on a civil judgment of fraud in dealing with a client. The court found that the superior court had not erred in denying the brokers' petition for a writ of mandate because the code sections were constitutional. The court found that the brokers had their day in the civil court where they were represented by counsel. It concluded that no due process violation occurred in having the evidence in the fraud action used in the Commissioner's hearing to revoke their licenses. Further, the brokers had an opportunity at the Commissioner's hearing to tell their stories. Section 10177.5 did not compel revocation. The Commissioner had discretion to continue, suspend, or revoke their licenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

1813 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Naumcheff


Crim. Nos. 920, 921


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


114 Cal. App. 2d 278; 250 P.2d 8; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1172



November 19, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County and from an order denying a new trial. Kenneth E. Morrison, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), upon a jury verdict, convicting him of grand theft and finding that he had a prior conviction of a felony in Oregon. He also appealed from an order denying a new trial. Defendant contended that Cal. Penal Code § 668 was unconstitutional, and the jury was improperly charged as to circumstantial evidence and impeachment of a prior felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbing two banks. In each information he was also charged with a prior felony conviction in Oregon for forgery, resulting in a term of imprisonment in that state. In rejecting defendant's argument that Cal. Penal Code § 668 was unconstitutional, the court held that the question was academic. No unconstitutionality appeared insofar as the statute affected defendant. He was not adjudged as a habitual criminal, and the provisions of § 668 had no direct application. Moreover, the matter of a prior conviction related only to punishment for a crime committed in California and to its use for purposes of impeachment. Both punishment and impeachment were matters for state determination, and the rules established applied to everyone alike. It was not error for the trial judge not to give an instruction on circumstantial evidence because there was sufficient direct evidence to sustain the verdicts. There was no prejudice to defendant in the trial court giving the jury an instruction to the effect that the fact that defendant had been convicted of a felony, if such was a fact, might have been considered in judging his credibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order of the trial court.

 

1814 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sheeter v. Lifur


Civ. No. 18950


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


113 Cal. App. 2d 729; 249 P.2d 336; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1439



October 20, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Harold W. Schweitzer, Judge.

Action to quiet title, in which one defendant filed a cross-complaint for similar relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant on cross-complaint affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax sale buyers challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which quieted title to the property in question in favor of defendants, allegedly delinquent taxpayers and railroad company, and enjoined the buyers from asserting any claims adverse to the railroad company, after the tax sale buyers brought a lawsuit to quiet title to the property.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the taxpayers and the railroad company after rejecting the buyers' argument that a tax deed established prima facie evidence of title in the buyers and also made out a prima facie case of nonpayment of taxes thereby casting on the taxpayers and railroad company the burden of proof as to payment of taxes. Specifically, the court held that whether the buyers' prima facie case was satisfactorily rebutted was a question of fact for the trial court's determination and that the record contained substantial evidence that the property was included in the taxpayers' operative property on which it paid a gross receipts tax for the year in question. Thus, the court held that such taxes were in lieu of all other taxes, making the property, in practical effect, exempt from additional assessments by the state or any of its subdivisions vested with taxing power, pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 14(a). Accordingly, the court concluded that the sale by the tax collector was unauthorized and void and the tax deed given in pursuance of such a sale conveyed no title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the taxpayers and the railroad company.

 

1815 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lewis & Queen v. S. Edmondson & Sons


Civ. No. 19031


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


113 Cal. App. 2d 705; 248 P.2d 973; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1434



October 17, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 16, 1952. Edmonds, J., Traynor, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred L. Bartlett, Judge.

Action on a labor and material bond given by contractor on public work.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, principal and surety, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which awarded plaintiff subcontractor the unpaid balance of the contract between the principal as general contractor and the subcontractor. The principal gave the subcontractor a labor and material bond. The award included attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor entered into a contract with the principal to do certain excavation work at the municipal airport. Defendants argued that it was error to admit parole evidence of the contract between the parties. The court found that the subcontractor furnished the material and performed the labor and services for which they sought compensation, the admission of parol evidence relative to the contract between the principal and the sub-contractor was immaterial because it did not affect the result of the litigation. The record was devoid of any evidence that the subcontractor or the principal did any work not required by the original contract, its plans and specifications, or authorized by proper change orders in accordance with the terms in the original contract. In addition, there was no abuse of discretion in fixing the attorney's fee because it was reasonable. The bond upon which the suit was instituted provided in part that in case an action was brought on the bond, the trial court would fix a reasonable attorney's fee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1816 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sullivan


Crim. No. 771


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


113 Cal. App. 2d 510; 248 P.2d 520; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1400



October 3, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied October 17, 1952, and Appellants' Petitions for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied October 30, 1952. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petitions Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of San Diego County and from orders denying a new trial and denying motions in arrest of judgment. John A. Hewicker, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to commit acts injurious to public morals and to pervert or obstruct justice or due administration of laws.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted them of conspiracy to commit acts injurious to public morals and to pervert or obstruct justice or due administration of laws, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 182(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy to commit acts injurious to public morals and to pervert or obstruct justice or due administration of laws, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 182(5). Defendants appealed their convictions, contending that the indictment did not state a public offense, and that § 182(5) was unconstitutional. The court held that the indictment fully advised defendants of the accusations against them. The court also held that the proven acts and conduct of defendants constituted an offense against public justice and the administration of laws. The court determined that, to make a statute sufficiently certain to comply with constitutional requirements, it was not necessary that it furnish detailed plans and specification of the acts or conduct prohibited. The court concluded that Cal. Penal Code § 182(5) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendants of conspiracy to commit acts injurious to public morals and to pervert or obstruct justice or due administration of laws. The court also affirmed the judgment denying defendants' motion for a new trial and motions in arrest of judgment.

 

1817 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Schaefer v. Superior Court of County of Santa Barbara


Civ. No. 19109


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


113 Cal. App. 2d 428; 248 P.2d 450; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1382



October 1, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County from pronouncing sentence until consideration of petitioner's application for probation.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandate granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner embezzler filed a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California) from pronouncing sentence until consideration of the convict's application for probation.


OVERVIEW: The embezzler was employed as an auditor by the state department of employment. He pled guilty to three counts of embezzlement. The embezzler filed a motion for probation. The trial court determined that it did not have jurisdiction to entertain the embezzler's application for probation. The embezzler filed a writ of prohibition, which the court granted. The embezzler was an employee, not a public official. Thus, he was not ineligible for probation under Cal. Penal Code §1203. Although the embezzler took an oath and furnished a surety bond as office manager and auditor in charge of a district audit office, the embezzler's position was subordinate to four other positions within the department of employment. The embezzler's position lacked elements which are usually associated with a "public office." He was not required, or authorized, to exercise a part of the sovereign power of the state. The embezzler was eligible for probation and was entitled to have his application for probation determined upon its merits.


OUTCOME: The court granted the embezzler's writ of prohibition to restrain the trial court from sentencing the embezzler before considering probation.

 

1818 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. Dallas


Civ. No. 4288


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


113 Cal. App. 2d 234; 248 P.2d 63; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1356



September 24, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 20, 1952. Carter, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. C. M. Monroe, Judge.

Action to restrain violation of Unfair Practices Act and for damages.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grocers challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which held in favor of defendant competitors in the grocers' action under the provisions of the Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code, § 17000 et seq., which sought restraint of the competitors from violating certain provisions of the act and damages.


OVERVIEW: The grocers leased premises near the competitors' market and began remodeling a building in which they commenced business as a market. The competitors owned and operated their store for nearly five years prior to when the grocers began remodeling. The grocers alleged that the competitors commenced selling various articles or products at less than cost for the purpose of injuring the grocers' business. On appeal, the grocers argued that the evidence did not support the findings of fact. The court found that the evidence established without question that the competitors advertised and sold certain grocery articles below cost. However, there was evidence that the competitors did not know that the grocers were opening their market until much later. The sale of the items below cost was made in good faith and not for the purpose of injuring the grocers. It was found that the grocers were damaged nominally, but the judgment was that the grocers take nothing. The findings of fact and the judgment were not inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the competitors was affirmed.

 

1819 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Barrows v. Jackson


Civ. No. 18717


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


112 Cal. App. 2d 534; 247 P.2d 99; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1061



August 6, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 4, 1952, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 2, 1952. Shenk, J., Edmonds, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Daniel N. Stevens, Judge.

Action for damages for breach of a covenant prohibiting use or occupancy of real property by non-Caucasians.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal on sustaining demurrer to complaint without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered judgment in favor of the appellee seller on the seller's demurrer in the appellant landowners' complaint against the seller for breach of a racially restrictive covenant, seeking damages for the diminution in value of the surrounding properties. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners and the seller entered into a restrictive covenant prohibiting occupation of their several parcels of land by any non-Caucasian persons. The seller conveyed a restricted parcel to a non-Caucasian and the landowners filed suit to enforce the covenant. Judgment was entered on the seller's demurrer. On appeal, the landowners claimed that the seller failed to include the valid and enforceable covenant in the conveyance. The court found (1) that there was privity of contract between the parties and that absent fraud, they were bound by the covenant unless it was contrary to public policy or violated a constitutional limitation, (2) that a restriction on the right of occupancy was a denial of equal protection that was prohibited by the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, (3) that judicial action to enforce the covenant was state action prohibited by the Fourteenth Amendment, (4) that the covenant, although valid, was unenforceable, and (5) that the denial of access to the courts for enforcement did not deprive the landowners of their property rights without due process because the landowners did not have the right to demand state action.


OUTCOME: The order sustaining the seller's demurrer to the landowners' claim that he had breached the valid racially restrictive covenant was affirmed.

Marlo v. State Board of Medical Examiners of Dep't of Professional Standards


Civ. No. 18776


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


112 Cal. App. 2d 276; 246 P.2d 69; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1017



July 18, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. William R. McKay, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review proceedings of State Board of Medical Examiners.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical doctor sought a writ of mandamus to the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which had affirmed the decision from respondent state board of medical examiners accusing the doctor of procuring, aiding or attempting to procure a criminal abortion. Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2377.


OVERVIEW: The medical doctor (doctor) sought a writ of mandamus to review proceedings from the state board of medical examiners (board), which had accused him of violating Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2377, in that he procured, aided or attempted to procure a criminal abortion. The doctor submitted a notice of defense, pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 11506. He was convicted and his license to practice medicine was revoked. The trial court denied him relief. He contended that the complaint filed against him did not state a cause of action; that Cal. Gov't Code §§ 11505 and 11506 were "inherently unconstitutional"; that the evidence was insufficient to support the findings; and that the court erred in the admission and inclusion of evidence. The court affirmed and held that the complaint displayed the violations in ordinary and concise language. It charged that he had performed an abortion on a specific date, with the name of the female victim provided. He was foreclosed from objecting to the form of the complaint on appeal where he failed to object in his notice of defense. The charging statutes properly provided for notice and hearing and were constitutional. Evidence was sufficient to convict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court, which had affirmed the decision of the state board of medical examiners accusing the doctor of procuring, aiding or attempting to procure a criminal abortion.

 

1821 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Oosterveen v. Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 18905


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


112 Cal. App. 2d 201; 246 P.2d 136; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1005



July 14, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 11, 1952, Edmonds, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Stanley Mosk, Judge.

Action to secure declaration of right to practice naturopathy without securing a license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment adverse to plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, graduate naturopaths and chiropractors (plaintiffs), challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment for defendants, State Board of Medical Examiners, State Board of Chiropractic Examiners, State Board of Osteopathic Examiners, and California Attorney General (defendants), in plaintiffs' declaratory action to secure a right to practice naturopathy without securing a license.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that naturopaths were subject to prosecution for practicing without a license, but that they could not, under existing laws, obtain a license to practice naturopathy. Therefore, plaintiffs contended that they were the subject of unjust and unconstitutional discrimination. The court held that it was within the legislative power to require naturopaths to acquire the education and pass the examination demanded of applicants for chiropractors' licenses, and that there was no undue discrimination against them. The court held that courts could not properly undertake the legislative and administrative functions that were involved in the regulation of the practice of medicine, surgery, and drugless healing. Further, the court held that they could not absolve naturopaths from the duty of complying with licensing statutes which established not only standard qualifications for applicants to practice, but also the procedure for testing their qualifications.


OUTCOME: In plaintiffs' action to secure from defendants a declaration that plaintiffs have a right to practice naturopathy without securing a license, the court affirmed the judgment for defendants.

People v. Albin


Crim. No. 4823


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


111 Cal. App. 2d 800; 245 P.2d 660; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1296



June 19, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County denying writ to attach body of appellant in state hospital and produce him at hearing of motion to annul order of commitment to hospital, and refusing to annul order of commitment. Ernest D. Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of orders by the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which denied defendant's writ to attach the body of defendant in a state hospital and produce him at a hearing on his motion to annul his order of commitment to the hospital. The trial court also refused to annul an order committing defendant to a state hospital after he was adjudged to be a sexual psychopath.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Cal. Penal Code § 288 on his guilty plea. Thereafter, defendant was adjudged to be a sexual psychopath and was ordered to be confined in a state hospital and returned to the trial court upon his release for further proceedings. Approximately three years later, defendant filed a motion to annul and vacate his commitment. Defendant also filed a motion for a writ of attachment commanding a sheriff to attach the body of defendant and produce him at the hearing on the motion to annul and set aside the commitment. The trial court denied both of defendant's motions. On appeal, the court held that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5502.5, pertaining to the procedure for defendant's release from the state hospital, was not unconstitutional. Defendant claimed that § 5502.5 was unconstitutional because it did not impose a duty on the hospital superintendent to form an opinion that defendant was no longer a menace to the health and safety of others. The court found that the intent of §5502.5, with respect to the superintendent's duties, rendered the language thereof mandatory and that the statute was neither vague nor uncertain, but a valid procedural statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

Hawthorn v. Beverly Hills

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders overruling demurrer and denying motion to quash temporary restraining order. Frank G. Swain, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel city to grant injured fireman leave of absence with full pay.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order refusing to quash temporary restraining order, affirmed; appeal from order overruling demurrer dismissed. Judgment granting writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and others, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which overruled their demurrer to petitioner fireman's mandamus proceeding to compel defendants to grant the fireman leave of absence with full pay, granted the writ of mandamus, and denied defendant's motion to quash a temporary restraining order under Cal. Lab. Code § 4850.


OVERVIEW: The fireman was injured on the job and was a member of the state employee's retirement system at the time of his injury. When defendants refused grant him a leave of absence with full pay pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 4850, he filed a mandamus action against defendants to compel the to do so. The trial court overruled defendants' demurrer to the suit, issued a temporary restraining order, and granted the writ of mandamus. The court held that mandamus was the proper remedy because there was no room for discretion in the defendants' performance of its duty under Cal. Lab. Code § 4850.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a writ of mandamus and the order refusing to quash temporary restraining order in the fireman's mandamus action to compel defendants to grant him leave of absence with full pay, and dismissed the appeal from the order overruling defendants' demurrer.

 

1824 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


General Electric Co. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 15115


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


111 Cal. App. 2d 180; 244 P.2d 427; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1632



May 19, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Opinion was Modified to Read as Above Printed and a Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 18, 1952. Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 17, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Thomas M. Foley, Judge.

Action to recover sales tax paid on turbine generator sold by manufacturer-installer to consumer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a turbine maker and its purchaser, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which held that respondent state Board of Equalization had properly taxed the transaction between appellants as a sale of personal property and denied appellants' claim for a refund.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a turbine maker and its purchaser, contracted for the construction and installation of an electrical turbine. The components were assembled out of state, then installed on real property owned by appellate purchaser in California. Respondent state Board of Equalization ruled that the transaction was a sale and denied appellants' claim for a refund. Appellants filed a lawsuit to recover the alleged overpayment of taxes. The trial court held that respondent had imposed the proper tax and denied the refund. Appellants sought review and the court affirmed. The court found that under Administrative Rule 11, Cal. Admin. Code § 1921, there was a distinction between structures and fixtures so far as contractors were concerned. A contractor who furnished a fixture that lost its identity primarily sold services, while a contractor who furnished a fixture that did not lose its identity sold tangible personal property. The court found this distinction to have been reasonable and nondiscriminatory. Thus, the court found that neither respondent nor the trial court had erred in having concluded that the turbine was tangible personable property and that the transaction was a sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that respondent state Board of Equalization properly taxed a transaction between appellants, a turbine maker and its purchaser, as a sale and denied appellants' claim for a tax refund. The court held that an administrative rule that distinguished between structures and fixtures was reasonable and that under the rule, a contractor that constructed, installed, and sold a fixture was a retailer of personal property.

 

1825 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pearson


Crim. No. 4749


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


111 Cal. App. 2d 9; 244 P.2d 35; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1612



May 9, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 20, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County denying a new trial. Arthur Crum, Judge.

Prosecution for violation of Gov. Code, § 6200, relating to interference with or removal of public records.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order denying defendant a new trial following a conviction, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of violating Cal. Gov't Code § 6200 and which denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a captain in the sheriff's office assigned to the vice squad. He was transferred to another division and had another officer remove portions of a file related to a gambling operation. The other officer returned the papers the next day and defendant was charged with violating Cal. Gov't Code § 6200, which prohibited altering or removing public records. He was convicted, and filed a motion for retrial. The motion was denied, and defendant sought review. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the trial court's denial of his motion for retrial. It found that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction because the honest inferences and indisputable facts established the guilt of the defendant. The fact that defendant ordered someone else to remove the file did not negate his culpability. Also, the records removed were public records as defined in the statute. It was not necessary for the state to prove that defendant intended to violate the statute because the statute imputed intent. Furthermore, there was no reversible error where the prosecutor asked improper questions and the trial court instructed the jurors to disregard the statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for interfering with public records and affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

1826 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Pacific Coast Engineering Co. v. State


Civ. No. 7991


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


111 Cal. App. 2d 31; 244 P.2d 21; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1613



May 9, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 3, 1952. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Jay L. Henry, Judge.

Action by seller of personal property against buyer for sales tax in addition to stated price.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant on sustaining demurrer to first amended complaint, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company appealed from the judgement of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sustained a general demurrer to the company's first amended complaint denying the company the right to collect sales tax on a contract in favor of respondent state of California.


OVERVIEW: The company and the state entered into a contract for goods and services. The contract specified an agreed upon price and was silent on the issue of sales tax. The company alleged that the sale price was exclusive of sales tax. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and stated that the company did not have the right to collect sales tax from the state in this instance because the contract was interpreted as to be the total sale price for the services provided by the company. The court found that Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 6052 allowed the imposed sales tax to be passed on to the consumer, but the amount of the tax should have been specified in the contract not presumed to be exclusive of the selling price. The court stated that there was no mandatory duty on the part of a retailer to collect the amount of the tax from the consumer. The court rejected the company's argument that Cal. Rev. & Tax code § 6053 required that sales tax be added as an additional charge to the selling price. The court determined that the right of a consumer to collect sales tax may be waived and, if it is not waived, it must be asserted upon the contractual agreements of the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the state in the action to collect sales tax.

Galli v. Brown


Civ. No. 14827


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


110 Cal. App. 2d 764; 243 P.2d 920; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1597



May 7, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 6, 1952, and Plaintiff and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 26, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from orders denying new trials. Sylvain J. Lazarus, Judge.

Action to recover, on behalf of city, salaries paid to certain city and county employees.



DISPOSITION: Portions of judgments involved on appeals by defendant and appellant, reversed; portions of judgments involved on appeals by plaintiff and appellant, affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed. Portions of judgments against defendant Edmund G. Brown, reversed; portions of judgments for defendants Harry D. Ross and John J. Goodwin, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer and defendant district attorney appealed judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in the taxpayer's action to recover salaries paid to two employees appointed by the district attorney. The trial court entered judgment for the taxpayer and awarded the city the amounts received by the employees as salaries. It also ruled in favor of defendants, the treasurer and the controller.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the appointment of the two employees was illegal because neither employee possessed the necessary qualification of two years' admission to practice law, as required by San Francisco, Cal., City & County Charter § 34. The trial court held that the two employments were illegal. It also found that the treasurer and the controller were not legally responsible for the illegal payments because they had paid the salary claims of the two employees in accordance with charter provisions. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment in part. The court held that the two were lawfully employed as warrant and bond clerks under San Francisco, Cal., City & County Charter § 30, and not as assistant attorneys. Section 30 clearly provided that the deputy in charge of the warrant and bond office did not act as the representative of the district attorney. The court held that the two years' service requirement was not applicable to either employee. While the court agreed that one of the employees did not meet the one-year city residency requirement, it found that the district attorney did not act in bad faith in making the illegal appointment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the judgment in favor of the treasurer and controller, who did everything required of them by the charter. The court reversed the portion of the judgment in which the trial court found that the appointments by the district attorney were illegal. The court dismissed the district attorney's appeal from the trial court's order denying his motions for a new trial because the orders were nonappealable.

Lewis Food Co. v. California Dep't of Public Health


Civ. No. 18759


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


110 Cal. App. 2d 759; 243 P.2d 802; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1596



May 6, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 28, 1952, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 26, 1952. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Philbrick McCoy, Judge.

Action for declaratory and injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff food company sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied the food company's request for declaratory relief and an injunction to restrain defendant Department of Public Health for the State of California from enforcing Cal. Health & Safety Code § 28007, which prohibited the use of certain terms on canned horse meat used for dog food.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the food company alleged that the trial court erred in finding that (1) the use of the words "with gravy" tended to mislead the public into the belief that dog food could be used for human consumption; (2) the food company's business would not be substantially affected by eliminating such wording from the labels; and (3) the food company was not deprived of its property contrary to due process of law. The food company further alleged that § 28007 did not bear a real or substantial relation to the object sought to be obtained and that it was arbitrary, unreasonable, and capricious, and, therefore, unconstitutional. People's Federal Savings & Loan Assn. v. State Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 18566


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


110 Cal. App. 2d 696; 243 P.2d 902; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1587



May 1, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 21, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Roger Alton Pfaff, Judge pro tem. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for refund of taxes paid under former Bank and Corporations Franchise Tax Act.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Franchise Tax Board (California) appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of plaintiff savings and loan association in an action for refund of taxes paid under the former Bank and Corporations Franchise Tax Act (the tax act), 1929 Cal. Stat. 19, as amended.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were mutual share building and loan associations organized under a state statute or mutual share savings and loan associations created under a federal statute. For two taxable years, the Board disallowed certain deductions and assessed additional franchise taxes. The trial court held that the limitation of the allowable deduction was unconstitutional and void. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court determined that there was no misjoinder because there was only one question of law, the validity of the assessments, and it was common to all plaintiffs. Second, the court determined that the portion of § 8(j) of the Act limiting the deduction of the return paid, credited on, or apportioned to the withdrawable shares to the average rate as determined by the building and loan commissioner was unconstitutional as a delegation of uncontrolled legislative power to an administrative officer to determine an average rate paid by all savings and loan associations in the state. The invalid portion of the statute was severable, and the deduction was permissible under the remainder of § 8(j) of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

1831 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Klassen v. Burton


Civ. No. 14994


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


110 Cal. App. 2d 539; 243 P.2d 28; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1567



April 28, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 28, 1952, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 26, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Murray Draper, Judge.

Action to recover salaries paid one defendant as city manager and to enjoin future payments.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) that was entered in favor of defendants, city manager and council members, in the taxpayer's action challenging the validity of a city ordinance that established a city manager form of government. The taxpayer sought to recover salaries paid to the city manager and to enjoin future payments to him.


OVERVIEW: The city council adopted a city ordinance to create and establish a city manager form of government. The ordinance provided that if any part of the ordinance was found to be unconstitutional, such decision would not affect the validity of the rest of the ordinance, and that the council would have passed the ordinance despite the unconstitutionality of any part of it. The ordinance also provided that due to the urgency of filling the vacancy of the office of city manager, the ordinance was effective immediately. The taxpayer brought an action challenging the ordinance's validity on the ground that the emergency clause was unconstitutional. The trial court upheld the ordinance. The taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed, holding that although the emergency clause was unconstitutionally void, it did not void the entire ordinance. The emergency clause was separable and hence the ordinance was otherwise valid. The court found that the language of the saving clause indicated that the council intended to adopt the ordinance even if the emergency clause was invalidated. The emergency clause was not an essential part of the ordinance and its invalidity did not destroy the entire ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, in favor of the city manager and members of the city council, in the taxpayer's action to challenge the validity of a city ordinance, to recover salaries paid to the city manager, and to enjoin future payments to him.
