San Francisco Brewing Corp. v. Johnson


Civ. Nos. 7983, 7984


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


110 Cal. App. 2d 479; 243 P.2d 53; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1557



April 22, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 9, 1952, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 19, 1952. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Percy West, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Actions to recover taxes paid on beer sold for export.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants on sustaining demurrers to complaints without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beer exporters sought review of orders from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sustained demurrers submitted by defendants, a state treasurer and others, without leave to amend to the exporters' actions to recover taxes paid on beer sold for export.


OVERVIEW: The state board of equalization levied additional assessments on beer produced by the exporters. The beer was exported and the exporters paid the additional assessments. The exporters then separately petitioned the board for reassessments, but that their petitions were denied on the sole ground that the exporters failed to comply with Cal. Bd. Equalization R. 54, Cal. Admin. Code, tit. 4, art. 10, § 54. The exporters filed complaints against the state treasurer and others seeking review of the dismissal of their petitions. The actions were consolidated and defendants demurred on the ground that the actions failed to state facts sufficient to constitute a cause of action. The trial court sustained the demurrers without leave to amend and the exporters sought review. The exporters argued that they were statutorily exempt from excise taxes on exported beer and that the board's rule could not destroy that exemption. The court found that the board's rule was within the authority delegated to the board and that it was not an invalid limitation of the statutory exemption. The court also found that the exporters' failure to comply with the board's rule acted as a waiver of the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1833 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Western Surgical Supply Co. v. Affleck


Civ. No. 7941


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


110 Cal. App. 2d 388; 242 P.2d 929; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1543



April 16, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 9, 1952, and Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 11, 1952. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to restrain members of State Board of Pharmacy from enforcing certain regulations and orders.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, drug distributor, requested a petition for a writ of mandate to restrain respondents, members of the California State Board of Pharmacy (board), from the enforcement of certain regulations and orders against the distributor.


OVERVIEW: The board caused criminal complaints to be filed against the distributor for violations of Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 20755, 29020, 29023 and Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 4030, 4161, 4231, 4232, 4233. While those charges were pending in various municipal courts, the board also served administrative notices of violations of its orders and regulations on the distributor. However, the board took no further action. The distributor claimed that the board's orders and regulations were invalid and filed a petition for writ of mandate to prohibit their enforcement. The court denied the petition because there was no jurisdiction where the board was not prosecuting the distributor. Until the board acted against the distributor, that is, conducted a hearing and rendered its decision, there was nothing to review or to prohibit. Whether the distributor violated the law or whether the board's orders were unconstitutional were questions beyond the scope of the court's proceedings because it would have been an interference with the criminal proceedings in the municipal courts.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandate against the board in the distributor's action to prevent the enforcement of the board's orders.

 

1834 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 14965


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


110 Cal. App. 2d 269; 242 P.2d 339; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1520



April 7, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Preston Devine, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco from proceeding further in an action.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco from proceeding further in an action against him for violations of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26286, the dissemination of false advertisements of drugs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that the statute under which he was being prosecuted was unconstitutional. He contended that Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26286 prohibited, but did not define, the dissemination of a false advertisement of a drug and that § 26271 declared false the advertisement of any drug represented to have an effect in certain enumerated ailments, irrespective of the truth or falsity in fact of the representation. The court found that this argument ignored § 26270, which declared that an advertisement of a drug was deemed to be false if it was false or misleading in any material particular. The first count of the complaint against appellant presented issues of fact under § 26270, not under § 26271. Thus, the petition did not challenge the jurisdiction of the municipal court to proceed under the first count. This was sufficient to deny the petition. Moreover, neither the second or third count of the complaint depended upon the constitutionality of § 26271. The municipal court could go forward under § 26270 on those counts charging false advertising.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying a wit of prohibition.

 

1835 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Roth v. Marston


Civ. No. 18632


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


110 Cal. App. 2d 249; 242 P.2d 375; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1516



April 4, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 29, 1952. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County granting a new trial. Charles F. Blackstock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which granted plaintiff a new trial based upon insufficiency of evidence but without so stating in the order.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a motion for a new trial, after defendant was awarded judgment. The trial court granted the motion based upon the ground of the insufficiency of the evidence to sustain the verdict and directed the clerk to enter the order as made in the minutes of the court. The clerk, however, entered the order that the motion was granted, without the trial court's reasons. Defendant appealed from the order. The trial court then made a nunc pro tunc order granting the motion for new trial and correcting the previous order's clerical error which did not conform to the its order for a new trial. The court reversed, holding that because the order did not specify that the motion was granted on the ground of insufficiency of evidence to sustain the verdict, it was conclusively presumed not to be based on that ground.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of a new trial to plaintiff because the order failed to state that a new trial was being granted based on insufficiency of evidence to support the verdict in favor of defendant.

 

1836 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mistriel


Crim. No. 4724


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


110 Cal. App. 2d 110; 241 P.2d 1050; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1492



March 27, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Otto J. Emme, Judge.

Prosecution for illegal possession of marihuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for illegal possession of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11500, entered in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). Defendant alleged that § 11500 was unconstitutional as being vague and ambiguous and that the evidence did not support the verdicts.


OVERVIEW: An undercover narcotics officer visited defendants' flower stand and asked to purchase marijuana. One defendant offered the officer a marijuana cigarette. Officers later searched defendants and their premises; they found marijuana on one defendant's person and on the premises. Defendants were charged with illegal possession of marijuana in violation of § 11500. The trial court found them guilty. On appeal, the court rejected defendants' argument that § 11500 was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous on the alleged ground that in prohibiting possession of a narcotic except by prescription, § 11500 related entirely to narcotics and could not be understood to apply to marijuana without reference to Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11001, which defined "narcotics" to include marijuana. The court held that § 11500 was clear and that it was not necessary that the definition of "narcotics" appear therein. Addressing defendants' argument that marijuana was not a narcotic but an herb, the court held that the legislature was empowered to enact § 11500 based on its rational belief that marijuana was a narcotic. Also, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdicts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for illegal possession of marijuana.

 

1837 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Perl


Civ. No. 15077


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


110 Cal. App. 2d 8; 242 P.2d 101; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1473



March 25, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco allowing claim of Department of Mental Hygiene for charges for maintenance of an incompetent person at a state hospital. T. I. Fitzpatrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the guardian of an incompetent person, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which allowed the claim of respondent, the Department of Mental Hygiene, for charges for maintenance of the incompetent at a state hospital. The Department brought the proceeding pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6655. The guardian was ordered to pay the charges.


OVERVIEW: The guardian was ordered to pay an amount that was greater than the actual cost of caring for the incompetent. The guardian claimed that § 6655 required the rate to be set at the actual cost of the care, support, and maintenance furnished. The rate assessed was based on the per capita cost of all of the inmates at the hospital, many of whom required a great deal more care. The court affirmed the assessed amount. The method of determining the rate was correct. Section 6655 had given the director of the Department the duty of fixing the rate but did not necessarily prevent a uniform rate for all patients able to pay although it told the director to fix it at "the actual cost." In 1933, the words "actual cost" were deleted from the statute. The state desired to make no profit from the care of its patients if all paid the rate so fixed. The basing of the rate upon per capita costs was more practical and less expensive than to keep books on each patient. The statute was not unconstitutional as returning a profit to the state because its purpose was to facilitate the efficient conduct of the state's business rather than to make a profit or to give something of value to another patient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1838 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Terry v. Civil Service Com.


Civ. No. 14795


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


108 Cal. App. 2d 861; 240 P.2d 691; 1952 Cal. App. LEXIS 1756



January 29, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. William T. Sweigert, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel municipal civil service commission to permit petitioners to take an examination for playground director.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment granting writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Civil Service Commission of the City and County of San Francisco (commission) sought to overturn the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which held that respondent applicants were entitled to a writ of mandamus ordering the commission to permit the applicants to take a civil service test.


OVERVIEW: The commission promulgated a rule specifying that it would only permit graduates of colleges accredited by two associations to take the civil service test for the position of playground director. The commission refused to accept applicants who graduated from institutions accredited by four other associations whose standards were virtually the same, and the lower court ordered the commission to permit the applicants to take the test prior to the issuance of a final decision. The lower court decided to granted a writ of mandamus in favor of the applicants, but before its findings were signed, the court was informed that all of the applicants had failed the civil service test. Nonetheless, the court granted the writ, and the court affirmed. The court ruled that the commission had acted arbitrarily and capriciously in promulgating its rule and that the rule violated the equal protection guarantees of the state and federal constitutions. The court held that the applicants' action was not moot because the applicants had requested the opportunity to take the test and not to pass it and because the rule would have been applicable to future examinations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which granted a writ of mandamus against the commission ordering the commission to permit the applicants to take civil service examination for the position of playground director.

 

1839 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Elbert, Ltd. v. Long Beach


Civ. No. 18307


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


108 Cal. App. 2d 463; 239 P.2d 4; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 2071



December 28, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Arnold Praeger, Judge.

Action to foreclose lien of a street improvement bond.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of respondent bondholder in the bondholder's action to foreclose a lien of a street improvement bond. The city failed to answer following the overruling of its demurrer to the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The bondholder owned a street improvement bond issued by the city. The bond was in default. The property that became subject to the lien of the bond was delinquent for state and county taxes. It was sold and deeded to the state. The state sold the property to the city. The bondholder alleged that the city's interest was subordinate to the lien of the bond. The trial court decreed that the property be sold and ruled that after the time allowed for redemption had expired, the city would be barred of all rights in the property. The city contended that the bondholder did not exercise its right to foreclose within the time allowed under Cal. Civ. Code § 2911. The bondholder argued that the lien of the bond was superior to the state's title and, therefore, did not come within the parity rule. The court found that the bondholder's right to enforce the lien of the bond had expired because the action was not commenced within the time prescribed by § 2911. Therefore, the demurrer of the city should have been sustained. Section 2911 made no distinction between a lien when there was parity and when there was not. It applied to all liens to secure payment of a public improvement assessment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Frazier v. Moffatt


Civ. No. 18375


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


108 Cal. App. 2d 379; 239 P.2d 123; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 2057



December 27, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 22, 1952, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 21, 1952. Carter, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Samuel R. Blake, Judge.

Action for false arrest and false imprisonment.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant judge appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that was in favor of plaintiff patron in an action for false arrest and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The judge and the patron were both dining at a cafe. At the time, the patron was laughing boisterously, and the judge, who claimed the laughter disturbed the peace, called the police and caused the patron to be arrested. The patron was acquitted of all charges, and he sued the judge for false arrest and false imprisonment. Judgment was entered in favor of the patron, and the judge appealed. The court reversed. Pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 838, the judge had a duty to cause the arrest of anyone committing or attempting to commit a public offense in his presence. When the judge acted pursuant to § 838 he did so within his jurisdiction and in the performance of a judicial act done in the execution of his office and within the purview of his general authority. Therefore, when so acting, the judge was not amenable to any civil action for damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the patron in his suit against the judge for false arrest and false imprisonment was reversed.

 

1841 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Chico v. First Ave. Baptist Church


Civ. No. 8035


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


108 Cal. App. 2d 297; 238 P.2d 587; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 2048



December 20, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County. Dudley G. McGregor, Judge.

Action to enjoin church and others from conducting a church or church services in a single residence zone.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a church and its members, appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which enjoined the church from conducting church services in a house located in an area zoned for single-family residential use. Plaintiff city objected to the house's use. The church argued that the decision, and local permit requirements, violated its members' constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action for injunctive relief against an area homeowner who was allowing a church to conduct worship services out of his home. Chico, Cal., Mun. Code § 1790(3) prohibited churches in areas zoned for single-family residential use unless the church obtained a special use permit. Chico, Cal., Ordinance 404 § 1796 created an action for abatement of a nuisance against landowners whose use of their premises were contrary to city laws. The church argued that the ordinance violated its members' constitutional rights to freedom of religious expression. The court explained that the church was a corporate entity organized under state law. Zoning ordinances were clear expressions of the state's police power, delegated by the state to the local government. The denial of a special use permit for a building did not prevent anyone from worshipping. But the church was required to obtain a special permit to do so in the disputed location. Although the church claimed to have applied for a permit, the court found that this was not the case. The church was required to exhaust its administrative remedies. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court held that the church was required to follow the city's zoning laws and abide by local permit requirements. The court observed that denial of a special use permit would merely prohibit the use of the house as a church; it did not prohibit church members from exercising their constitutional rights to worship as they chose. The court affirmed.

Stryker v. Republic Pictures Corp.


Civ. No. 18256


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


108 Cal. App. 2d 191; 238 P.2d 670; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 2029



December 13, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 7, 1952. Carter, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. William B. McKesson, Judge.

Action for damages for invasion of privacy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants on sustaining demurrer to complaint, and plaintiff's election not to amend complaint, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ex-soldier appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that sustained defendant motion picture corporation's general and special demurrer to the ex-soldier's action for damages for invasion of privacy.


OVERVIEW: The ex-soldier, who participated in the Iwo Jima invasion during World War II, filed a complaint against the motion picture corporation that alleged that a motion picture reenacted and depicted incidents, conditions, and circumstances he encountered, which was a violation of his state right of privacy. The trial court sustained the motion picture corporation's general demurrer to the complaint, as well as its special demurrer to the complaint (both with leave to amend) that sought to elicit from the ex-soldier to what extent, if any, that the picture represented fictional activities on his part, rather than his actual activities. The ex-soldier elected not to amend on the theory that none of the grounds set forth in the demurrer was well taken. The trial court entered judgment for the motion picture corporation on the sustained demurrer, and the court affirmed. The court held that members of the military subjected their military, but not personal, activities to the public gaze. The court found that the ex-soldier's complaint was vulnerable to demurrer in that it relied upon the right of privacy for the ex-soldier's actual military activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment in favor of the motion picture corporation where the trial court sustained the general and special demurrer to the ex-soldier's complaint, and the ex-soldier's election not to amend his complaint that sought damages for invasion of privacy.

Perez v. San Jose


Civ. No. 14766


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


107 Cal. App. 2d 562; 237 P.2d 548; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1946



November 16, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Byrl R. Salsman, Judge.

Action by taxpayer to determine right of city to use tax funds for improvement of part of a state highway within city's boundaries.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) in favor of defendant city in the taxpayer's action that sought a determination as to the city's right to use tax funds for improvement of part of a state highway within the city's boundaries.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action challenging the city's use of tax funds for the improvement of part of a state highway that was within the city's borders. The trial court determined that the city was entitled to use tax funds for such an improvement, and the taxpayer sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's finding that the city was entitled to use tax funds for such an improvement. The court found no indication of legislative intent to limit the cities in the construction and maintenance of state highways within their boundaries to state funds. The court also found that Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 113 expressly permitted the use of any funds that the city might properly use for the construction and maintenance of its own streets. The court held that the city and its inhabitants received a special benefit, as compared with the rest of the state, in the improvement of the state highway that was within the city limits; therefore, such an improvement was a municipal purpose. The court ruled that because this city street was also a state highway made it no less a city street and made its improvement no less a matter of city concern.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the city was entitled to use tax funds for improvement of a state highway that was within the city's boundaries.

People v. Hess


Crim. No. 4337


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


107 Cal. App. 2d 407; 237 P.2d 568; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1922

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 20, 1951, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 6, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying a new trial. Frank G. Swain, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to embezzle public funds and for fraudulent appropriation or secretion of public property by state officer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied their motions for a new trial after they were convicted of conspiracy and substantive charges of embezzlement, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 504, and corruption, in violation of Cal. Gov't. Code § 14420.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for their involvement in a scheme to share in inflated prices for parcels of real estate purchased with public funds for road construction. The court affirmed the convictions. The court rejected defendants' contention that the jury was not a fair cross section of the community. The court ruled that: (1) defendants' appropriation of the excess profit for their private use constituted a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 504; (2) when viewed in conjunction with the overt acts charged, the allegations of the indictment were sufficient to inform the accused of the charges they would be required to meet at the trial; (3) the amended indictment was not deficient in any of the essentials of a valid accusation, being framed in the words of the statute; (4) the inclusion of an alternate juror preserved the three essentials and substantive attributes or elements of a trial by jury, that is, number, impartiality and unanimity; and (5) the jury was properly instructed as to the applicable law. The court ruled that defendants received a fair and impartial trial and that their conviction rested upon legal and substantial evidence.

Estate of Hart


Civ. No. 18370


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


107 Cal. App. 2d 58; 236 P.2d 884; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1854



October 24, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 18, 1951. Carter, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a part of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County omitting provision for costs in favor of proponents of will after a judgment refusing revocation thereof, and from orders amending the judgment and striking the cost bill. Harold B. Jeffery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Part of judgment appealed from affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executors contested that part of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which omitted a provision for costs in favor of the will's proponents after a judgment refusing revocation thereof. The executors also appealed the trial court's orders amending the judgment and striking the cost bill. Respondent contestant had challenged the executors' propounding of the decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: After a jury sustained the decedent's will, a judgment denying a petition for revocation of the will was filed containing a provision that the will's proponents could recover their costs and disbursements from the contestant. Upon the contestant's motion, the trial court struck the provision for costs from the judgment. Cal. Prob. Code § 383 provided that a will contestant had to pay the costs of trial if the probate were not revoked. The court found that if § 383 were held to be mandatory, it would be contrary to the requirement of Cal. Const. art. I, § 11 that all laws of a general nature had to have a uniform operation. No logical or reasonable basis existed for mandatorily awarding costs against a contestant after a will was admitted to probate and not awarding the same costs against a contestant before the will was admitted to probate. The court concluded that, by construing the statute as merely directory, it was consistent with the constitutional provision. Thus, the trial court correctly struck the provision from the judgment and made an order leaving the determination of costs until there had been a final determination of the litigation on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the trial court's judgment from which the appeal was taken. The court dismissed the purported appeals from the order of the trial court amending the judgment and the order striking the cost bill.

Clopton v. Scharrenberg


Civ. No. 18258


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


106 Cal. App. 2d 430; 235 P.2d 84; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1765



August 31, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a minute order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County dismissing an amended petition for writ of mandate after a demurrer thereto was sustained. W. Turney Fox, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel payment of petitioner's salary as referee of Industrial Accident Commission during absence for performance of ordered naval duty, and compensation for vacation and holding time during such absence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Minute order of dismissal, entered pursuant to order sustaining demurrer to amended petition, reversed insofar as it dismissed petition as to count on salary issue, and affirmed insofar as it dismissed petition as to vacation and holiday time issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the minute order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained defendant employer's demurrer and dismissed his petition for a writ of mandate to command the employer to pay his salary for the time he had missed during January of the year he returned to work from serving in the military and to restore his vacation and holiday privileges from the time he was gone.


OVERVIEW: After working for his employer, a state agency, for a few years, the employee was absent on active duty as a commissioned officer of the United States Naval Reserve. He returned to work several years later and missed some time in January, but less than 30 days. Cal. Mil. & Vet. Code § 395 provided that state employees who had worked more than 1 year shall not have had any loss or diminution of vacation or holiday privilege and who were absent less than 30 days per year shall have received their salary for that time. The trial court found in favor of the employer. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court found that the section was to be liberally construed. The court concluded that the cause of action for his salary was not barred by the statute of limitations because it did not accrue until after the end of the year, which was the earliest point at which he could have known that he was absent less than 30 days. The court found that although his vacation and holiday privileges could not have been diminished because of his absence, he did not receive the privilege during his absence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's minute order to the extent it dismissed the employee's petition on the salary issue but affirmed the trial court's order to the extent it dismissed his petition on the vacation and holiday issue.

Jones v. Maloney


Civ. No. 14657


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


106 Cal. App. 2d 80; 234 P.2d 666; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1717



August 15, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Daniel R. Shoemaker, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel vacation of orders revoking petitioner's licenses as an insurance agent and an interinsurance agent.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying petition, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner agent appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate to vacate orders made by respondent insurance commissioner revoking the agent's licenses as an insurance and interinsurance agent.


OVERVIEW: After filling out the required forms, the agent received licenses as an insurance and interinsurance agent. On the forms, the agent indicated that he had never been convicted of a misdemeanor. However, he had two misdemeanor convictions for disturbing a public assemblage and disturbing the peace and resisting an officer. The commissioner revoked the agent's licenses, finding that he knowingly made a misstatement and obtained each license by concealment and misrepresentation. The agent filed a petition for a writ of mandate to vacate the revocation order, which the trial court denied. The court reversed, finding that although there was evidence to support a finding that the agent knowingly misrepresented the convictions, the charge of concealment could not stand because there was no evidence that the misrepresentation had any bearing on his obtaining the licenses; the offenses were ancient and bore no relation to his qualifications for a license. In addition, because the commissioner made a single order of revocation based on his conclusions that both charges had been substantiated, the court remanded to the commissioner for reconsideration of the penalty for the first charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which denied the agent's petition for a writ of mandate to vacate the commissioner's orders revoking the agent's licenses. The court directed the trial court to enter judgment commanding the commissioner to set aside his order of revocation and to reconsider the penalty for the first charge of knowingly making a misstatement.

 

1848 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


American Transit Mix Co. v. Weber


Civ. No. 7962


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


106 Cal. App. 2d 74; 234 P.2d 732; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1716



August 14, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Sherrill Halbert, Judge.

Actions to foreclose materialmen's liens and to quiet title.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgments for defendants in foreclosure actions, reversed; judgment for plaintiff in quiet title action, modified so as to declare his title to building subject to liens thereon.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lienholders sought review of decisions of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), which did not allow liens against respondent owner's lot and building and quieted title in favor of the owner. The lienholders had filed actions against the owner and the materials requester to foreclose materialmen's liens. The owner had filed a quiet title action against the lienholders and the materials requester.


OVERVIEW: The lienholders filed separate actions against the owner and the materials requester to foreclose materialmen's liens. The owner answered the lienholders' complaint by asserting the non-responsibility defense under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1192. The superior court rendered judgment against the material requester, but did not allow liens against the owner's lot and building. The owner then filed a quiet title action against the lienholders and the materials requester. The superior court quieted title in the owner against the lienholders and the materials requester. The lienholders appealed the superior court's decisions. The court reversed the superior court's judgments for the owner in the foreclosure actions and modified the judgment for the owner in the quiet title action through declaring the owner's title to the building subject to the lienholders' liens. The court held that the superior court erred in disallowing the liens, as the termination of the land purchase contract by the decree in the quiet title action did not nullify the lienholders' liens against the building.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment for the owner in the lien foreclosure action that was initiated by the lienholder. The court modified the superior court's judgment for the owner in his quiet title action by declaring his title to the building subject to the lienholders' liens. The court also remanded the cases to the superior court for further proceedings in accordance with its opinion.

 

1849 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Copeland v. Kern County


Civ. No. 4329


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


105 Cal. App. 2d 821; 234 P.2d 314; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1552



August 3, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 27, 1951, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 1, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Stanley Murray, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to enjoin construction of a county highway or expenditure of money in such construction except in conformity with law.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California) that was in favor of defendants, a county and county officials, in an action to enjoin the construction of a county highway or the expenditure of money for such construction.


OVERVIEW: The county began construction of a new county highway. The work was done by county employees and farm camp prisoners. The taxpayer, believing that using both of these types of labor was prohibited by law, filed an action to enjoin the construction project or the expenditure of funds for the project. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of defendants, and the taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed. Under Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 2009, the county's board of supervisors had broad powers with respect to county highway matters, and in referring to the hiring of employees, § 2009 expressly stated that the board of supervisors could approve salaries and compensation to be paid. This was sufficient to authorize the county to use its regular road crews in the construction project. Further, the term "day labor" as used in Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 1075 meant for the employment of all persons necessary to complete a project. This did not impose a restriction upon the use of the regular road crew.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1850 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gordon


Civ. Nos. 14640, 14696


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


105 Cal. App. 2d 711; 234 P.2d 287; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1536



July 30, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County granting a temporary restraining order, denying motion to discharge such restraining order, and from minute and formal orders granting a preliminary injunction. Byrl R. Salsman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Formal order granting a preliminary injunction modified and affirmed; appeals from other orders dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state brought an action against defendant grocer under the Unfair Trade Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17000 et seq. (the Act). The Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) granted a temporary restraining order against the grocer, denied his motion to dissolve the order, entered a minute order granting a preliminary injunction, and then formally issued a broader preliminary injunction. The grocer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state's action was based on violations of §§ 17043 and 17044 of the Act, which prohibited selling products below cost and using products as "loss leaders." The grocer claimed that the minute order disposed of the state's case and that the Act and its application violated the Commerce Clause and equal protection and conflicted with the Sherman Act. The state claimed that it did not purposefully discriminate against the grocer and that relevant limitations of the Act should be considered incorporated in the injunction. The court held that the minute order was not a final disposition of the state's action, as it did not detail the acts prohibited. The Act did not regulate interstate commerce but was a valid exercise of the state's police power. The Act did not conflict with the Sherman Act, as it did not address price fixing. The Act was uniform in application; the grocer might have been the first in his area against whom action was taken but did not show that the state purposefully discriminated. As the injunction did not limit its prohibition on selling below cost to conduct that had a purpose to injure competitors, the injunction had to be modified to comply with the Act.


OUTCOME: The court modified the preliminary injunction to add the words "if such act is done for the purpose of injuring competitors or destroying competition." The court affirmed the preliminary injunction against the grocer, as modified, and dismissed the grocer's appeals of all other orders.

 

1851 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Diaz


Crim. No. 4616


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


105 Cal. App. 2d 690; 234 P.2d 300; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1532



July 27, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 6, 1951, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 23, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County and from an order denying a new trial. R. R. Sischo, Judge assigned. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Prosecution for murder.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction of first degree murder, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California) for murder in the first degree, asserting that the trial court committed reversible error in refusing to allow defendant the number of peremptory challenges to which he was legally entitled pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1089.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried for murder for shooting and killing the 17-year-old daughter of his nephew. During voir dire, a jury of 12 was chosen and the trial court began the selection for an alternate juror without first swearing in the jury, as required under § 1089. During the selection of the jury, defendant used 18 of the 20 peremptory challenges allowed by Cal. Penal Code § 1070. He then exercised two more peremptory challenges during the selection of the alternate. When another potential alternate was subjected to voir dire, defendant sought to use another peremptory. The trial court denied the request, holding that defendant has used his 20 peremptories. The alternate was sworn in with the jury. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error in denying defendant the peremptory challenge afforded him under Cal. Penal Code § 1089, which allowed one peremptory for each alternate. In total, defendant had 21 peremptories available to him. The fact that he exercised two of them during the selection of the alternate did not preclude his right to exercise his final peremptory challenge. By denying him this right, the trial court unconstitutionally denied him a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first degree murder.

 

1852 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


Crim. No. 4635


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


105 Cal. App. 2d 701; 233 P.2d 633; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1533



July 27, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 2, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Percy Hight, Judge pro tem. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Prosecution for incest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), convicted defendant of two offenses of incest upon his daughter. Defendant appealed form the trial court's judgment and from its order denying his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because the victim's testimony was incredible and because her testimony conflicted with that of an examining physician. In affirming the conviction, the court found nothing indefinite in the victim's testimony. Nor was there anything in her narration of the occurrences that was unbelievable. Further, the fact that the testimony of an examining physician indicated that the victim had engaged in sexual activity only recently contradicted the victim's testimony that she had been submitting to defendant for over two years did not render the victim's testimony unreliable. The physician's testimony gave substantial support to the victim's testimony as to the commission of the crimes on the dates charged. The court concluded that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1853 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pollack


Crim. No. 4631


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


105 Cal. App. 2d 581; 234 P.2d 176; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1512



July 24, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 31, 1951, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 23, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Clement D. Nye, Judge.

Prosecution for violating Pen. Code, § 337a, subd. 1, forbidding pool selling or bookmaking.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), denying his motion for a new trial pursuant to his conviction for violating Cal. Penal Code § 337a(a) in engaging in bookmaking activities.


OVERVIEW: After following defendant to several locations, city police officers arrested him as he entered the home of a woman whose name was found on a betting slip with an amount noted that corresponded with the amount the woman informed police she owed defendant in bets on horses. On defendant's person, the officers confiscated betting slips, an owe sheet, scratch sheets, and a daily racing form. At trial, the State's expert described betting operations and the documents and papers used therein. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court should have defined the term "to engage" as meaning activity that was continuous in nature and connoting more than a single act. He also argued that there was insufficient evidence to sustain his conviction. In finding otherwise, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction and held that Cal. Penal Code § 237a made it clear that a single violation thereof constituted the proscribed offense. Further, § 237a was not so vague that a person of ordinary intelligence could not understand the meaning of terms such as "bookmaking" and "pool-selling" as such terms were well understood in modern society. Finally, the evidence supported the jury's finding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction entered by the trial court.

 

1854 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lord v. Henderson


Civ. Nos. 17237, 17238, 17239, 17240


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


105 Cal. App. 2d 426; 234 P.2d 197; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1489



July 16, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 13, 1951. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from a special order directing payment of money held in a special fund. Harry R. Archbald, Judge.

Actions for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgments for plaintiffs reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff transporters filed an action against defendants seeking to have the Caravan Act of 1937 declared unconstitutional. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of the Caravan Act of 1937 (Act) which imposed a fee upon caravans traveling inter-and intrastate as well as vehicles being transported for sale being driven into state individually and not as part of a caravan. Plaintiff asserted that the Act violated the commerce clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, infringed the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment, and violated the uniformity and the privileges and immunities clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 11 and 21. One plaintiff transported his vehicles in tandem caravans, and the others transported them individually. The trial court entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the statute's classification and tax of vehicles transported on the state's highways for gain was proper even though it did not create any additional traffic hazard or undue wear and tear than vehicles not transported for gain; the legislature had the authority to regulate commercial and noncommercial traffic differently.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments in favor of plaintiffs and against defendants, holding the Act unconstitutional, were reversed.

 

1855 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Keddy


Crim. No. 4656


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


105 Cal. App. 2d 215; 233 P.2d 159; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1451



June 29, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of indecent exposure, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 311, and lewd and dissolute conduct, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 647.5. The matter was certified to the superior court (California) pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5501, and petitioner was remanded to the sheriff's custody. Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus for his release from custody. The court granted bail pending a hearing upon the writ.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus for either his discharge from custody on the ground that § 5501 was unconstitutional, or for his release on bail pending a determination of whether or not petitioner was a sexual psychopath. The court granted bail pending a hearing on the writ. The court held that § 5501 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause or Due Process Clause and was constitutional. Petitioner was not being placed twice in jeopardy for the same offense because a commitment proceeding under § 5501 was civil in nature, not criminal. A person committed pursuant to § 5501 was not confined for the commission of a crime but because he was a sexual psychopath. A sexual psychopath was not an insane person. Petitioner was entitled to bail pending his appeal from the denial of his motion for a new trial after his misdemeanor convictions. The court granted the writ and ordered that petitioner was entitled to be released on bail pending the determination of whether or not he was a sexual psychopath because Cal. Const. art. I, § 6 provided that all persons were bailable by sufficient sureties, unless for capital offenses when the proof was evident or the presumption great.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of habeas corpus. The court ordered that petitioner was permitted to remain on bail pending the determination of the superior court as to whether or not petitioner was a sexual psychopath.

 

1856 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. Bauer


Civ. No. 14547


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


104 Cal. App. 2d 740; 232 P.2d 590; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1682



June 14, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. M. G. Del Mutolo, Judge.

Action for specific performance of agreement to transfer liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant general partners sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted plaintiff limited partners specific performance of an agreement to transfer a liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The general partners pledged a liquor license to the limited partners as security for the payment of a loan. After the general partners defaulted on the loan, the limited partners filed an action against them based upon a limited partnership agreement that provided for the transfer of the liquor license to the limited partners in such an event. The trial court granted specific performance of the agreement, and the general partners appealed. The court affirmed the judgment against the general partners. The court held that § 7.3 of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act (1949) did not prevent specific performance of the agreement because the limited partners' right to the liquor license accrued prior to the enactment of § 7.3. The court found that a sworn statement required under § 7.3 was not necessary for specific performance of the transfer agreement under the circumstances. The court concluded that the evidence supported the trial court's finding that the transfer of the limited partners' interest in the license to the general partners at the time of making the loan was adequate consideration for the agreement and that the agreement was additional security for the loan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the general partners that granted specific performance of an agreement to transfer a liquor license to the limited partners.

 

1857 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hess


Crim. No. 4336


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


104 Cal. App. 2d 642; 234 P.2d 65; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1674



June 12, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 25, 1951, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 12, 1951. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from order denying a new trial. Frank G. Swain, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to embezzle public funds.



DISPOSITION: Two judgments affirmed; appeal from other judgment dismissed. Judgments of conviction affirmed as to defendants John K. Hess and William E. Rose; appeal of defendant Royall W. Wheeler from judgment dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) convicted defendant state officials of conspiracy to violate Cal. Penal Code § 504. Defendant real estate broker's proceedings were suspended and he was placed on probation. The superior court denied the motions of all defendants for a new trial and for a judgment of acquittal. All defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state officials were state right-of-way agents charged with procuring property from individuals for the right-of-way of the Hollywood Freeway in the city of Los Angeles. The state officials allegedly provided the real estate broker with information as to the properties located in the right-of-way. The real estate broker contracted with individual property owners to sell their home before the property owners were approached by the state. The real estate broker split his commission from the sales with the state officials. A jury composed of 11 women and 1 man did not violate defendants' constitutional rights to a fair trial. The state officials alleged that they were entitled to acquittal on the charge of conspiracy because they were acquitted on the charge of embezzlement that arose from the same facts. The court held that the state officials were not entitled to acquittal on the charge of conspiracy because the substantive crime of embezzlement and the crime of conspiracy were separate and distinct offenses. The court held that the trial court did not err in replacing a juror with an alternate juror after the juror's father suffered a stroke.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of the state officials for conspiracy and affirmed the superior court's denial of defendants' motions for a new trial and for acquittal. The court dismissed the real estate broker's appeal of probation.

 

1858 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Oil Workers International Union v. Superior Court of Contra Costa County


Civ. No. 14088


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


103 Cal. App. 2d 512; 230 P.2d 71; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1204; 28 L.R.R.M. 2643; 20 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P66,545



April 18, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING to review an order of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County finding petitioners had violated a temporary restraining order and adjudging them in contempt. Hugh Donovan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to certain acts of contemnors and annulled as to other acts of contemnors.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, union, affiliated organizations, and members, appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) that held that petitioners violated a temporary restraining order and adjudged them in contempt. This order was issued in an action brought by respondent company to enjoin the commission of certain activities by petitioners in their strike of respondent company.


OVERVIEW: Respondent company brought an action to enjoin petitioners, union, affiliated organizations, and members, from destroying property and intimidating people during a strike. Respondent court entered a temporary restraining order (TRO) to enjoin this activity and subsequently held that petitioners violated the TRO and adjudged them in contempt of court. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Although a few judgments were reversed because the complaints did not allege the commission of acts enjoined by the TRO, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the majority of the judgments. The TRO did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I and was applicable to petitioners, union and affiliated organizations, because the definition of "person" in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 17 was not restricted to "natural persons." The Labor Management Relations Act of 1947 and the National Labor Relations Act of 1935 did not preclude respondent trial court from enforcing its TRO. The court's inquiry was limited to jurisdiction, and it could not consider the affidavits used to support the subpoenas duces tecum. Finally, oral arguments were a privilege, and respondent company was properly joined.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent trial court's order, which found that petitioners, union, affiliated organizations, and members, violated a temporary restraining order and adjudged them in contempt. Although a few judgments were reversed because the complaints did not allege the commission of acts enjoined by the TRO and thus did not implicate respondent trial court's jurisdiction, the evidence was sufficient to sustain most of the judgments.
