Record v. Indemnity Ins. Co.


Civ. No. 14624


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


103 Cal. App. 2d 434; 229 P.2d 851; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1193



April 13, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco denying attorneys' fees. Preston Devine, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff and his attorneys appealed from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that denied attorney fees. Plaintiff asserted an entitlement to the same under Cal. Lab. Code §3856.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff hired attorneys to pursue an injury action. After a successful recovery, a lien holder that had a stake in the outcome of the case refused to pay plaintiff's counsel any fees for the recovery of their interest. The plaintiff and his attorneys were initially denied the fees and they appealed. On appeal the court reviewed the applicable subrogation provisions of the insurance statutes. The court concluded that an amendment which addressed the issue in question was not effective at the time of the claim. Further, since there was no agreement against the appropriation of attorney fees the grant of the same was proper. Therefore, the decision was reversed and remanded for fee determination.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to the trial court to determine attorney fees because the applicable contract in the case had not excluded any right to seek attorney fees.

 

1860 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Mefford v. Tulare


Civ. No. 4078


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


102 Cal. App. 2d 919; 228 P.2d 847; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1409



March 19, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 12, 1951, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 17, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Frank Lamberson, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiff reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which granted declaratory relief to respondent subdivision developer, holding that a city ordinance that required the developer to provide a profile map of proposed subdivision drainage was null and void as against the developer and enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance against him.


OVERVIEW: The developer owned a tract of land in the city, which he planned to subdivide. Under a city ordinance, he was required to submit a profile map to the city for approval by the city engineer, indicating where he proposed to place drainage for sewage. The developer brought a declaratory action to test the validity of the ordinance. The trial court held that the ordinance was adopted as an initiative measure without appropriate power in the electors of the city and granted the developer declaratory relief, declaring the ordinance null and void as against the developer and enjoining the city from enforcing the ordinance against him. The city appealed, contending that declaratory relief was inappropriate and that the ordinance was a valid exercise of electors' power. On appeal, the court reversed, ruling that although declaratory relief was appropriate, adoption of the ordinance was a valid exercise of the electors' powers under the city charter and the court did not find anything in the general laws of the state that limited such powers. Thus, the trial court erred in declaring the ordinance null and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which granted declaratory relief to the developer, declared the city ordinance null and void, and enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance against the developer.

 

1861 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dierssen v. Szmidt


Civ. No. 4080


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


102 Cal. App. 2d 743; 228 P.2d 317; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1378



March 8, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 3, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Arthur C. Shepard, Judge.

Action to quiet title.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant original owner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which entered a judgment quieting title to certain lots acquired by tax sale to plaintiff purchaser.


OVERVIEW: In 1925, the property was sold to the state for nonpayment of taxes. It was deeded to the state on June 30, 1930. Notice of sale was published on December 3, 1937 and the county tax collector mailed a copy of the notice to the original property owner. The original property owner never received the letter sent by the county tax collector and had no knowledge of the sale until 1939. The purchaser acquired the property as the success in interest to the person who bought the property at the public auction. No physical occupancy of the property was ever effected by the parties or the lessee. In 1945, the purchaser commenced a quiet title action. The trial court entered a judgment for the purchaser and the original property owner appealed. The court affirmed and determined that the lack of notice to the original property owner was cured by the statute of limitations. The court found that the original property owner was barred from challenging the validity of the tax deed to the state and could not raise the invalidity of the tax deed in her action to quiet title to the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that quieted title to the property in the purchaser.

 

1862 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Reihs


Civ. No. 17913


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


102 Cal. App. 2d 260; 227 P.2d 564; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1305



February 13, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 5, 1951, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 12, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. John Gee Clark, Judge.

Proceeding for determination of interest in a decedent's estate.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant half-cousin sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, California, from an order denying a new trial. The trial court adjudged that bequests to German charitable institutions and respondent United States Attorney General, as successor in interest to three named German legatees, were entitled to distribution of bequests made to them under the will.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was a United States citizen and California resident. Decedent's will made certain bequests to United States residents and charities. The half-cousin was granted a legacy. Decedent also provided bequests to several German charities and three named German legatees. Decedent died in 1946, shortly after the close of World War II. On appeal, the court found that the Attorney General, as successor in interest, relied on his vesting order and sought distribution to himself of the legacies to the three German citizens. The court found that pursuant to Cal. Prob. Code § 259 the German legatees would be ineligible to take under the will if German wartime law prohibited United States citizens from taking under German wills. In affirming, the court found that German law in 1946 provided for a reciprocal right to United States citizens to take by inheritance personal property or proceeds under the same terms and conditions as German residents and citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that determined decedent's estate was to be distributed according to his will, in favor of German charitable institutions and the Attorney General, as successor in interest to three named German legatees. The court dismissed the half-cousin's appeal from the order denying a motion for new trial.

 

1863 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. Hobba


Civ. No. 17728


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


102 Cal. App. 2d 170; 227 P.2d 57; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1288



February 6, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 5, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clarence M. Hanson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel city officials to issue a license for a private patrol system.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment granting writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a mayor and city officials, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held in favor of plaintiff owner in a proceeding in mandamus to compel city officials to issue a license for a private patrol system.


OVERVIEW: The owner of a private patrol system and was duly licensed and engaged in the business of guarding private property for compensation in the city. The city passed and adopted Signal Hill, Cal., Ordinance 311, which required a permit from the city council and license fees. The city council denied the owner's application for a permit on the ground that he had previously been arrested and had a record. A new ordinance was passed. The owner filed an amended petition for mandate. The city answered that the owner had not complied with the new ordinance and that by reason of its passage prior to the filing of the owner's amended petition, the matter was moot. The trial court ordered a peremptory writ requiring the city to issue a license or to show cause in reference thereto. The court affirmed. The trial court, after duly considering the arguments presented, rendered judgment ordering the city to issue the license. The trial judge considered and weighed the various opposing propositions. The burden of pointing out a reason for reversal rested upon the city. The court held that the city showed no abuse of discretion to justify a reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1864 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


C. Dudley De Velbiss Co. v. Kraintz


Civ. No. 14178


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


101 Cal. App. 2d 612; 225 P.2d 969; 1951 Cal. App. LEXIS 1058



January 8, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County. Hugh Donovan, Judge.

Action for a declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for defendant reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) in favor of defendant a county building inspector in an action for declaratory judgment that sought a declaration that Contra Costa County, Calif., Bldg. Ordinance 385 was invalid and that the company was not required to comply with the provisions of the ordinance. The trial court sustained a general demurrer to the complaint filed by the inspector.


OVERVIEW: The company, which was in the home building business, attacked Ordinance 385 and the amendments to Ordinance 385 in numerous respects and for various reasons. The company contended that Ordinance 385 did not intelligibly classify buildings subject to its own regulatory provision, that there was an inter-mixture of zone lines, dates of subdivisions, legal method of subdivision, type of operation, and type of property, that it was not only discriminatory in its application but was vague and indefinite. The court held that it did not need to pass on the specific questions of unconstitutionality urged by the company further than to determine that there were justiciable questions suggested which could not have been determined in the absence of evidence of the actual facts existing in the county which may or may not have made the classifications of the ordinances under attack reasonable or unreasonable. The court found that the company's complaint suggested constitutional questions, which the court could not say lacked merit on the facts alleged. The court concluded it was prejudicial error to sustain the demurrer without granting the company leave to amend the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with directions to permit the company to file an amended complaint if the company so requested.

 

1865 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sevier v. Bank of America National Trust & Savings Assn.


Civ. No. 14473


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


101 Cal. App. 2d 184; 225 P.2d 3; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1094



December 18, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Ralph E. Hoyt, Judge.

Proceeding for administration of the estate of a missing person.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment ordering defendant to pay to plaintiff money payable to missing person under terms of a trust, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank held property in trust for a missing person. The bank sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which ordered it to pay to plaintiff administratrix money payable to the missing person under the terms of a trust and pursuant to California's scheme for the administration and ultimate distribution of the estates of missing persons, Cal. Prob. Code §§ 280-294.


OVERVIEW: The bank challenged the constitutionality of the statutory scheme on the grounds that it did not satisfy due process requirements. The bank argued that that unless the property was seized before the administration commenced, the statutes were required to provide for the restoration of the property to the missing person whenever he reappeared, after however long a period. In affirming the judgment, the court concluded that the bank's argument placed too great emphasis on the purely mechanical. After the lapse of three years of administration (or of one if the missing person had been unheard of for 10 years prior to commencing the proceedings), the statutory scheme provided for a final distribution and barred the missing person's rights by limitation. The court found that the statutory scheme's time limits were not unreasonable and its provision for notice was adequate.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering the bank to pay to the administratrix money payable to missing person under terms of the trust was affirmed.

 

1866 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Richfield Oil Corp. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 17603


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


100 Cal. App. 2d 535; 224 P.2d 398; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1250



November 20, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 18, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. William J. Palmer, Judge.

Action for refund of solvent credits tax paid under protest on amount in excess of balance of accounts receivable and accounts payable.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and a county, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which awarded respondent taxpayer a refund of solvent credits tax paid under protest on the amount the taxpayer held in excess of balance of accounts receivable and accounts payable. The trial court found that the federal agencies doing business with the taxpayer were bona fide residents of California under Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer had accounts receivable from agencies of the United States government of $ 4 million and accounts payable to the same agencies of $ 2 million. A solvent credits tax was levied by the city and the county against the full amount of accounts receivable, without deduction of accounts payable. The taxpayer paid under protest and later was awarded a refund. The trial court found that the agencies were bona fide residents of California and that the taxpayer's taxable solvent credits due from the agencies were $ 1.8 million, representing a net balance owing to the taxpayer. The court affirmed on appeal, finding no error. The court found that Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1, was constitutional. The legislature could permit taxpayers to deduct the debts due to persons doing business in California. Thus, the taxpayer had properly taken the deductions. The taxpayer also properly filed his statement under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 1060; no balance sheet was needed. It was the duty of the assessor to credit the taxpayer for its bona fide debts. Failing in that duty, it was the province of the trial court to make the deduction and to declare the amount of the tax, which it did.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below.

 

1867 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sogawa v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 17360


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


100 Cal. App. 2d 181; 223 P.2d 269; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1186



October 27, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clarence M. Hanson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Motor Vehicles to rescind an order suspending a chauffeur's license.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting writ, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the California Department of Motor Vehicles and its director, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that, in a proceeding in mandate brought by plaintiff driver, ordered defendants to rescind an order suspending the driver's chauffeur's license.


OVERVIEW: The question on appeal was whether defendants had authority to revoke the driver's license. The ground of suspension was that the driver was involved in an automobile accident and had failed to deposit security in the amount demanded by the Department of Motor Vehicles. The driver argued that all the provisions of the financial responsibility statutes which referred to licenses of "operators," were properly construed as applying to "operators' licenses" but not to "chauffeurs' licenses. Reversing, the court held that the driver's contention that the Department of Motor Vehicles was without authority to suspend his chauffeurs' license had no support in the applicable provisions of the California Vehicle Code. Even if the driver was able to prove that he was a chauffeur, as defined by Cal. Veh. Code § 71, and was acting as such at the time of the accident, such proof would not have entitled him to a judgment directing the restoration of his suspended license. The financial responsibility requirements applied to the licenses of all operators of vehicles, whether they were operators' licenses or chauffeurs' licenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1868 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sindell v. Smutz


Civ. No. 17424


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


100 Cal. App. 2d 10; 222 P.2d 903; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1156



October 17, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 14, 1950. Traynor, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Joseph W. Vickers, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel issuance of an oil permit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment directing issuance of writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning administrator appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that granted a writ of mandate to compel issuance of an oil permit to petitioners, lessees under an oil lease in an oil field, under Los Angeles, Cal., Ordinance 94,136 (Nov. 12, 1936), which provided that not more than two wells could be drilled in each city block.


OVERVIEW: The oil field was in the City of Los Angeles. Wells were permitted, drilled, and spaced at one well to an acre. Affirming, the court concluded, as a matter of law, that the ordinance was unduly oppressive and not reasonably necessary to promote the general welfare of the community. The reasonableness of the ordinance was not fairly debatable and the facts did not show a case where there may be a difference of opinion on the subject. The exercise of legislative power exceeded constitutional limitations. The ordinance did not afford adequate means of protection as a substitute for the right to drill an offset well. It deprived the lessees of their right, coequal with the right of other owners and lessees in the oil field, to recover their fair share of the oil from the common source of supply and, consequently, infringed upon the constitutional guaranties invoked. There was no equality of production. When the block was considered as a whole, at least another well was needed thereon to prevent discrimination and confiscation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1869 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Morganti v. Morganti


Civ. No. 7746


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


99 Cal. App. 2d 512; 222 P.2d 78; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1738



September 20, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sonoma County. Donald Geary, Judge.

Action for divorce.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former wife brought an action to obtain a divorce from defendant former husband upon the ground of his alleged incurable insanity. The Superior Court of Sonoma County (California) granted the wife an interlocutory decree of divorce. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife failed to allege that she had reasonable ability to support the husband for the remainder of his life expectancy or that he had sufficient property to provide such support as required by Cal. Civ. Code § 108. Nevertheless, the trial court overruled the husband's demurrer to the complaint on this ground because it declared the foregoing requirement of § 108 to be unconstitutional. The court agreed. The court held that a classification could not be arbitrary. It had to be based upon some difference in the classes having a substantial relation to a legitimate object to be accomplished. The requirement at issue in § 108 constituted a classification based on financial ability which was without reasonable relation to either of the legislative objects of (1) providing a manner of proof where the ground for divorce was incurable insanity, or (2) securing financial support for the insane spouse. Such classification was an arbitrary denial of equal protection and was invalid. The remainder of § 108 could be given effect and a divorce granted on the ground of incurable insanity.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decree by striking that portion of the decree which purported to relieve the wife from her obligation of support. The court then affirmed the decree as modified.

Helvey v. Security-First Nat'l Bank


Civ. No. 17334


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


99 Cal. App. 2d 149; 221 P.2d 257; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1671



August 22, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County dismissing an amended complaint. Charles F. Blackstock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator of an estate of a deceased depositor sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which dismissed his amended complaint to recover property under the Abandoned Property Act, Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1274.1 to § 1274.17, against defendant successor bank upon the bank's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Depositor made certain deposits in a predecessor bank. After almost 20 years and no withdrawals or deposits being made in the account, the successor bank paid the amount due on the account to the treasury of the state under the Abandoned Property Act. While the administrator's proceeding was pending against the state under Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1274.10, he commenced the current action against the successor bank because he allegedly could not recover interest from the state. The administrator made no appearance on the hearing of the motion to dismiss. Because no evidence before the trial court was supplied to the court, it was presumed that the evidence supported the order. The administrator argued that the trial court's order was not based on facts specified in Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 581 et seq. and was, therefore, void. The court held that the trial court had inherent power to dismiss actions which were made to appear fictitious and sham. The court also held that the administrator's arguments challenging the constitutionality of the Abandoned Property Act were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

1872 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Garner v. Board of Public Works


Civ. No. 17411


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


98 Cal. App. 2d 493; 220 P.2d 958; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1885



July 19, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 8, 1950, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 13, 1950. Gibson, C. J., Carter, J., and Traynor, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County denying alternative writ of mandate. Clarence M. Hanson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel reinstatement of discharged municipal employees and payment of salaries from date of their discharge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant discharged municipal employees sought review an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied the employees' alternative writ of mandate to compel respondent board of public works to reinstate them and to pay their salaries from the date of their discharge.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance in which all employees were to take an oath of loyalty to the city, wherein all employees were to represent that they did not, for five years prior to the affirmation, work for an agency that sought the overthrow of the government. Seventeen employees refused to take the oath and were terminated. They filed a petition for a writ of mandamus and sought reinstatement and back pay. The trial court denied their petition. The employees sought review. The court affirmed judgment and held that: (1) loyalty was indispensably necessary in the employer-employee relationship between the state and its servants; (2) it was treasonable to advocate the destruction of the government for which they worked; (3) it was a duty of those charged with managing the government to ascertain, require, and insure unconditional, unswerving loyalty of every servant of the people, high or low; and (4) the ordinance was well within the legislative power of the city and was timely exercised.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied the employees' alternative writ of mandate to compel respondent board of public works to reinstate them and to pay their salaries from the date of their discharge.

 

1873 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Raffington


Crim. No. 4441


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


98 Cal. App. 2d 455; 220 P.2d 967; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1877



July 14, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 10, 1950. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles W. Fricke, Judge.

Prosecution for abortions and attempted abortion.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of attempted abortion and abortion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted abortion and abortion. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, defendant contended that he was denied due process of law in that he was charged by an information filed by the district attorney and not by indictment of the grand jury. The court held that: (1) the words "due process of law" in the Fourteenth Amendment did not require an indictment by a grand jury in a prosecution by a state for a felony, and a conviction upon an information filed by the district attorney did not deprive a defendant of life, liberty, or property without due process of law; (2) contrary to defendant's contention, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the trial court's judgment; (3) defendant's contention that he was entrapped was not sustained by the evidence; (4) entrapment was available as a defense when a criminal design originated with an officer who, by persuasion or deceit, enticed a law-abiding citizen to commit a crime that he would not have committed in the absence of such inducement; and (5) whenever the design of a person to commit a crime was clearly shown, slight acts done in furtherance of the design would constitute an attempt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1874 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Perez


Civ. No. 17680


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


98 Cal. App. 2d 121; 219 P.2d 35; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1813



June 15, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 10, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County appointing an administratrix. Alfred E. Paonessa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the surviving children and heirs at law of a decedent, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which appointed respondent, the decedent's wife, administratrix of the decedent's estate. The children filed a contest to the wife's application for letters of administration on the ground that she was not the lawful widow of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The wife was refused a health certificate sought for the purpose of obtaining a marriage license because the examining physician found her to be afflicted with a communicable disease. A month later, the wife and decedent were married in Arizona in accordance with the laws of that state, and returned the next day to California where they lived until the decedent's death less than a year later. The children alleged that the marriage of the wife and the decedent was void because it was contracted between the parties for the specific purpose and with the specific intent of evading the laws of California. The court rejected the children's contention, holding that if California residents were married in another state in conformity with the laws of that state, even if their marriage in California would have been invalid, and they entered the other state with the avowed purpose of evading the laws of California, such motive did not invalidate the marriage. The court held that the marriage of the wife and the decedent, because it conformed with the laws of Arizona, was a valid marriage. The court rejected as inapplicable several cases cited by the children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Penaat v. Zeiss


Civ. No. 14214


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


97 Cal. App. 2d 909; 219 P.2d 60; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1634



June 9, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 8, 1950, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 3, 1950. Carter, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to review proceedings of Contractors State License Board suspending license of a contractor. Theresa Meikle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment denying relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor filed suit, in mandamus, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5 to review by mandate the Contractors' State License Board's decision suspending for one year his license as a contractor. The superior court (California) sustained the board's decision. The contractor challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The charges against the contractor stemmed from accusations that he violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 7116, 7114 and 7119. On appeal, the contractor argued §§ 7116, 7114 and 7119 were unconstitutional, that the accusations were insufficient, and that the evidence did not support the findings of guilt. Specifically, the contractor claimed that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7116 was unconstitutional because it made any act which was "wilful or fraudulent" a subject of disciplinary action and that, since it was penal in its nature, it did not define the "crime" with sufficient particularity. The court held that § 7116 was not a penal statute and the rules covering due process in criminal proceedings therefore did not apply. Likewise, the court held that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7114 and 7119 were not penal statutes. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence substantiating the allegation that the contractor charged an unlicensed builder a fixed commission for the use of his license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision sustaining the board's decision to suspend the contractor's license for one year.

 

1876 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garcia


Crim. No. 2605


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


97 Cal. App. 2d 733; 218 P.2d 837; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1602



May 25, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from an order denying a new trial. Edward P. Murphy, Judge.

Prosecution for violation of the Deadly Weapons Act.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possessing a deadly weapon after being convicted of a felony, in violation of the California Deadly Weapons Act (Act), 1923 Cal. Stat. 695, entered in the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California). Defendant argued, among other things, that the Act violated his constitutional right to bear arms and that he was subjected to an unconstitutional search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a companion, while driving in a car, were followed by police officers whose suspicions were aroused. The officers stopped the car for investigation. As one officer opened a door of the car, he saw defendant slip a gun under his seat. While questioning defendant, the officers learned that he was on parole for a felony conviction. Defendant was convicted for possession of a deadly weapon as a convicted felon, in violation of the Act; the trial court denied his motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court held that the Act did not violate defendant's right to bear arms under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1 because the Act was a proper exercise of the State's police power in protecting the welfare of society. Further, in addressing defendant's argument that there was a variance between the information and the proof in that the information charged that he owned and possessed the gun but there was no proof of ownership, the court found that the Act was worded in the disjunctive, so that proof of possession alone was sufficient; thus, defendant was not prejudiced by the information's wording. Also, the officers' warrantless search and seizure was not improper under the facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a deadly weapon after having been convicted of a felony; the court also affirmed the order denying defendant's motion for a new trial.

Brooks v. Stewart


Civ. No. 4073


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


97 Cal. App. 2d 385; 218 P.2d 56; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1543



May 5, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 12, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. Strother P. Walton, Judge pro tem. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel county clerk to accept and file petitioner's nomination papers for a public office.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an incumbent official holding the county office of coroner and public administrator, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which dismissed the official's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent, a county clerk, to accept his nomination papers for the office.


OVERVIEW: The official presented nomination papers for the office of coroner-public administrator. The clerk refused to accept the papers on the basis that the office was eliminated by two ordinances enacted by the board of supervisors pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 24300. The trial court sustained the clerk's demurrer to the official's petition for a writ of mandate. The official argued that the ordinances were void and that § 24300 left the question of consolidation of county offices to the board of supervisors and was therefore an unconstitutional delegation of powers under Cal. Const. art. XI, § 5. The court affirmed, finding that § 24300 was not unconstitutional. The statute did not attempt to delegate the legislative power to create a public office, fix the terms of the office, or prescribe the duties of the office. The statute did not lack uniformity of operation. The fact that the ordinances did not first separate the officers before the consolidations was not material. The court held that a public hearing was not required for a finding of public interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which denied the official's petition for a writ of mandate to compel the clerk to accept and file his nomination papers.

Dairy Belle Farms v. Brock


Civ. No. 14275


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


97 Cal. App. 2d 146; 217 P.2d 704; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1500



April 25, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Milton D. Sapiro, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel Director of Agriculture to set aside order suspending petitioner's milk license.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting writ, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Director of Agriculture sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which entered judgment directing the director to set aside his order suspending respondent dairy farms' milk license for three days and remanding certain proceedings to the director for further consideration.


OVERVIEW: An accusation was filed with the director charging that the dairy farms had violated the provisions of Cal. Agric. Code § 736.13. The director found the dairy farms guilty and ordered their distribution license suspended for three days. The dairy farms filed a petition for a writ of mandate in the trial court and obtained an alternative writ staying the operation of the order of suspension. The trial court entered judgment vacating the director's order of suspension and remanding the proceedings. The director appealed and the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court correctly found that the dairy farms, in order to contract with the City and County of San Francisco, were required to comply with § 736.13 but incorrectly found that the dairy farms had substantially complied with it and also incorrectly found that § 736.13 did not require filing prices five days before making an offer to sell. The trial court also incorrectly ordered the matter remanded to the director. The court held that the dairy farms had not complied with § 736.13 and therefore the director was justified in finding that they had violated § 736.13 and in ordering the three-day suspension.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted the writ ordering the director to set aside his order suspending the dairy farms' license for three days and remanding the case.

California State Auto. Asso. Inter-Insurance Bureau v. Downey


Civ. No. 14078


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


96 Cal. App. 2d 876; 216 P.2d 882; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1460



April 10, 1950

Proceeding in mandamus to compel Insurance Commissioner to restore petitioner's right to do business.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automobile insurance association appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that denied the appellant's petition to compel the insurance commissioner to restore the right to do business after it failed to comply with an Assigned Risk Plan.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a service oriented automobile association which subsequently wrote automobile insurance policies for it's members. The insurance was available only to their members. Fortier Transp. Co. v. Union Packing Co.


Civ. No. 16953


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


96 Cal. App. 2d 748; 216 P.2d 470; 1950 Cal. App. LEXIS 1438



March 30, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders granting a new trial and a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Charles P. Johnson, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for damages arising out of a collision of vehicles.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; order granting new trial affirmed; appeal from other order dismissed. Judgment for defendants notwithstanding a verdict for plaintiff, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) in favor of defendants, a corporation and its driver, in a tort action. The trial court also ordered a new trial on defendants' cross-complaint.


OVERVIEW: Four motor vehicles were involved in an accident. Plaintiff's vehicle was known as a tanker, and defendants' vehicle was a cattle truck and trailer. On appeal, plaintiff argued that the trial court erred in overturning its verdict. The court reversed the judgment notwithstanding the verdict and ordered a new trial on all issues. In doing so, the court held that there was evidence that both sides violated provisions of the motor vehicle code. However, the trial court did not instruct the jury relative to speed and other provisions of the code. Whether the speed of plaintiff's or of defendant's vehicle was the proximate cause of the damage, or was a bar to recovery because of contributory negligence of either driver, were jury questions that were not fully and fairly considered by the jury. Accordingly, the appellate court exercised its discretion to order a new trial on all of the issues. The court also determined that the JNOV was without support because of substantial evidence in the record to show the negligence of defendant's driver.


OUTCOME: The order granting a new trial as to part of the issues was affirmed. The JNOV was reversed. The appeal from the order granting the motion for JNOV was dismissed. The action was remanded for a new trial on all of the issues.

 

1882 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bradford


Crim. No. 4378


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


95 Cal. App. 2d 372; 213 P.2d 37; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1123



December 28, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Charles W. Fricke, Judge.

Prosecution for bookmaking resulting in a conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment convicting defendant of bookmaking, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 337a(1), and denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court rejected defendant's attack on the constitutionality of § 337a. The terms "pool-selling" and "bookmaking" were so well understood that no person of ordinary intelligence could have misunderstood the import and meaning of the terms. These terms were of general use, and they had a well-accepted and recognized meaning throughout many jurisdictions. The court concluded that the term "bookmaking" clearly meant the making of a betting book. Further, the court rejected defendant's argument that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. The evidence showed that at the time of defendant's arrest he was in possession of all the paraphernalia and equipment necessary to perpetrate the crime of bookmaking as denounced by § 337a(1). He had in his possession all of the paraphernalia commonly used by bookmakers in plying their trade. He was possessed of scratch sheets, owe sheets, and betting markers, the presence of which constituted the major element of the crime charged. The court concluded that logical and proper inferences could be drawn that such paraphernalia was being used for bookmaking purposes.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's attempted appeal from the judgment and affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

1883 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rhode Island Ins. Co. v. Downey


Civ. No. 14210


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


95 Cal. App. 2d 220; 212 P.2d 965; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1105



December 21, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 16, 1950. Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco to vacate its order appointing conservator of business and assets of insurance company, and restraining company from carrying on its business.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance company sought to vacate an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), granting respondent, the state insurance commissioner, conservatorship over petitioner in an action under Cal. Ins. Code § 1011.


OVERVIEW: Respondent insurance commissioner applied for a writ naming him conservator of petitioner insurance company under Cal. Ins. Code § 1011. Respondent requested conservatorship in order to enjoin petitioner from transacting further business in the state. Petitioner filed an alternative writ requesting that the lower court be directed to vacate the order granting respondent's writ. Petitioner argued that respondent's actions were arbitrary and unnecessary. The court denied petitioner's alternative writ, holding that respondent's allegations supported his contention that he was justified. The facts did not establish abuse of discretion and respondent was not limited to taking action only in an urgent emergency situation. Alternative remedies suggested by petitioner were either equally drastic and injurious to petitioner, or did not provide adequate protection to the policyholders and the public. The fact that respondent's writ was granted without prior notice and hearing did not violate due process because the public interest required immediate action.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request to vacate the order granting respondent conservatorship because respondent was within his proper authority in taking action to halt petitioner from conducting business in the state.

People v. Luse


Crim. No. 4370


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


95 Cal. App. 2d 200; 212 P.2d 582; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1101

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 16, 1950. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles W. Fricke, Judge.

Prosecution for forgery and for recordation of false or forged instruments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of forgery and of recordation of false or forged instruments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant altered, without authority, stock certificates of a corporation and filed or caused to be filed for record, numerous false or forged documents. Defendant was convicted of forgery and of recordation of false or forged instruments. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed the convictions. The court found that there was substantial evidence to sustain the judgments of guilty. There was also substantial evidence to show that the crimes were committed in the forum county within three years prior to the filing of the informations. The statute of limitations had not run on the offenses. The trial court had limited defendant, at trial, to one counsel. Defendant challenged Cal. Penal Code § 1095, the statute by which the trial court had been governed. The court held that § 1095 was constitutional. The trial court had not committed prejudicial error in refusing to allow defendant to be represented before the jury by more than one counsel. The trial court also did not commit prejudicial error in denying defendant's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of forgery and of filing false documents.

Mitchell v. Morris


Civ. No. 17192


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


94 Cal. App. 2d 446; 210 P.2d 857; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1556



November 3, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clarence M. Hanson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel city building superintendent to issue a building permit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an applicant for a building permit, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent, the Superintendent of the Department of Building and Safety of the City of Los Angeles, to issue the applicant a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The Superintendent refused to issue the building permit because the lot on which he sought to build a dwelling house did not front upon a public street nor upon a private easement that the city planning commission determined to be adequate as required by Los Angeles, Cal., Zoning Ordinance § 12.03. The applicant argued that the planning commission wrongfully, arbitrarily, and capriciously refused to approve a private easement and that § 12.03 was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to the planning commission. The trial court held no hearing and took no evidence when it denied the applicant's petition. On appeal, the court found that the city could properly prohibit the construction of a dwelling on property that had no access to a public street or an adequate easement when the city was concerned with access to a house by the fire or police department. The court interpreted § 12.03 as granting the planning commission authority to grant a variance from the requirement of having access to a public street where a private easement served as an adequate substitute, and operation under § 12.03 was not an exercise of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the applicant's petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

1886 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Department of Social Welfare v. Gardiner


Civ. No. 3974


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


94 Cal. App. 2d 431; 210 P.2d 855; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1554



November 2, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 22, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Joe L. Shell, Judge.

Action against estate of deceased recipient of old age relief to recover double amount of aid paid to decedent during a designated period.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff on overruling demurrer to complaint and defendant's failure to answer, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executor challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) for respondent Department of Social Welfare in the Department's action to recover, under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 2223, double the amount of old age security aid paid to the decedent during a specified period.


OVERVIEW: Upon decedent's death, it was discovered that he had money and personal property in excess of the amounts allowed for a recipient of old age security aid. The Department made a claim against the estate for double the amount of improperly received aid under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 2223 and, after he refused the claim, brought suit against the executor. The trial court denied the executor's demurrer and, after the executor refused to answer, rendered a judgment for the Department. The court affirmed. The court refused to accept the executor's contention that § 2223 was unconstitutional as a bill of attainder. While the double recovery was in the nature of a penalty and did not become effective until the decedent's death, the decedent was neither deprived of a trial nor adjudged a criminal. In order for the Department to recover, certain facts had to be judicially established and the penalty was effective against the decedent's estate rather than the decedent. Noting that the penalty was imposed both to further the desired ends of the benefit law and to secure compliance with it, the court found that the imposition of this penalty was within the legislative power of the state.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment for the Department was affirmed.

 

1887 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


B. C. Turf & Country Club, Ltd. v. Daugherty


Civ. No. 14013


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


94 Cal. App. 2d 320; 210 P.2d 760; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1532



October 28, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 26, 1949, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 22, 1949. Shenk, J., Voted for a Hearing. Gibson, C. J., did not Participate.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Stanley Murray, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel Corporation Commissioner to rescind an order and a letter.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment denying writ, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco denying a writ of mandate to set aside an order prohibiting appellant from selling its stock in California and to rescind a letter sent to all brokers ordering them to refrain from trading appellant's stock.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment denying a writ of mandate to rescind an order prohibiting appellant from selling its stock in California and to rescind a letter sent to all brokers prohibiting them from trading appellant's stock. The court reversed the judgment and found appellant did not violate the California Corporate Securities Act because appellant's actions did not constitute a solicitation of a sale or a preliminary negotiation requiring a permit. The Act required a foreign corporation to secure a permit before soliciting a sale, or to engage in preliminary negotiations looking towards a sale. The court found the statute was not applicable because it did not prohibit the general discussion of a business organization. The court rejected respondent's argument that appellants were acting as agents of the corporation because there was no evidence of agency. The court also found since the letter was predicated on the order, it must fall with the order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying the writ of mandate because appellant did not violate the California Corporate Securities Act.

 

1888 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Scherbing


Crim. No. 2547


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


93 Cal. App. 2d 736; 209 P.2d 796; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1453



September 23, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 20, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County and from an order denying a new trial. Edward I. Butler, Judge.

Prosecution for unlawful possession of a weapon by a prisoner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which convicted him of possessing a dagger or sharp instrument while committed to a State prison, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 4502. Defendant also appealed the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not deny that he had been found to possess a homemade sharp-pointed knife with a 5 1/2-inch blade sharpened along one side. As a juvenile offender, defendant had been committed to the State prison by the California Youth Authority after he was convicted of second degree burglary at the age of 18 years. He alleged that he was not a prisoner "committed" to a State prison within the meaning of § 4502. The court found the argument to be fallacious. A "commitment," in the legal sense, could be lawfully issued by other than a judicial body. The Penal Code gave the Authority the lawful power to make orders transferring prisoners under their supervision from one state institution to another. Next, the court held that the fact that defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor, not a felony, did not make his commitment to the State prison by the Authority unlawful. Cal. Penal Code § 5077 and other statutes authorizing the Authority to make such commitments were not unconstitutional. Lastly, even if defendant had been unlawfully confined, Cal. Penal Code § 4502 still applied. An unlawful commitment did not confer upon defendant the right to possess weapons denied to other inmates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Payne v. Real Estate Comm'r


Civ. No. 7655


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


93 Cal. App. 2d 532; 209 P.2d 419; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1417



September 6, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 3, 1949. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing. Gibson, C. J., did not Participate.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Malcolm C. Glenn, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel restoration of broker's real estate and business opportunity licenses.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants on sustaining demurrer to petition without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner real estate broker (broker) appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sustained a demurrer to the broker's petition against respondent, the Real Estate Commissioner of the State of California (commissioner), to compel the commissioner to restore the broker's real estate license and his business opportunity license.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner revoked the broker's real estate license and business opportunity license based on his violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 10177(b), (f), 10302(b), (e). The broker had been convicted of bigamy. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the revocation of the broker's licenses under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 10177(b), 10302(b) was legally proper because the commissioner could have suspended or revoked the licenses of a broker who had been convicted of a felony, knowledge of which the commissioner did not have at the time of last issuing a real estate license to him. The court did not agree with the broker's contention that Cal. Bus. & Prof. §§ 10177(f), 10302(e) were void for uncertainty and unconstitutional. The court explained that because the statutory standards of truth, honesty, and good reputation had been held to be constitutional in license application cases, it followed that they were constitutional insofar as the lack of those qualities constituted a cause for disciplinary action under §§ 10177(f), 10302(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the commissioner's demurrer to the broker's petition against the commissioner to compel him to restore the broker's real estate license and his business opportunity license.

Palaske v. Long Beach


Civ. No. 16799


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


93 Cal. App. 2d 120; 208 P.2d 764; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1357



July 29, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 18, 1949, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 26, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Thomas J. Cunningham, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city to pay a policeman an annual pension.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment granting writ modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and officials, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent policeman a writ of mandate compelling the city to pay him an annual pension equal to 50 percent of his annual salary plus 1-2/3 percent of his annual salary for each year of service over an aggregate of 20 years.


OVERVIEW: The policeman worked for the city for 17 years, served in the armed forces for three years, and was reinstated to his former position upon discharge. The policeman worked for another two years and then applied for a retirement pension pursuant to 1931 Cal. Stat. 2785, § 187(2), which was denied because he had not served 20 years "in the aggregate" as a member of the police department. The court found that the policeman was entitled to credit for the time served in the armed forces because at the time he entered the military, there was an established practice on the part of those that administered the pension program to include leaves of absence in computing "aggregate" service. The court also found that the city had the power to modify the pension plan and that 1945 Cal. Stat. 2954 § 187.1 effectively limited the policeman's pension right to 50 percent of his salary. The court modified the award by striking the part that granted the policeman 1-2/3 percent of his annual salary for each year of service over 20 years because he could not earn any additional pension above that to which he was entitled on the effective date of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment that awarded mandamus relief to the policeman by striking the portion of the writ that compelled the city to pay him as part of his annual pension 1-2/3 percent of his annual salary for each year of service over an aggregate of 20 years. The court affirmed the judgment as modified, which compelled payment of an annual pension equal to 50 percent of the policeman's annual salary.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted following a jury trial of forgery, offering false or forged documents to be filed of record, and offering false evidence. The court also held that it was error to submit an instruction permitting a finding that defendant endeavored to procure false or fabricated evidence to be produced at the trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a new trial.

1894 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stucker v. Katz


Civ. No. 14066


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


92 Cal. App. 2d 843; 207 P.2d 879; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1771



July 15, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 13, 1949, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 12, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Thomas M. Foley, Judge.

Action to recover arrears of alimony from personal representative of deceased husband.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former wife sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which found that her remarriage resulted in the termination of her deceased husband's estate's obligation to pay her alimony. The trial court had based its finding upon an amendment to Cal. Civ. Code § 139 (amended 1933). The wife had filed an action against defendant, a personal representative of the estate.


OVERVIEW: The wife had procured a decree of divorce from the deceased husband in 1926. She was awarded monthly alimony. After his death in 1945, the wife sued the representative for the accrued balance of alimony. The trial court found that the wife had remarried in 1937, and that be reason of such remarriage the alimony obligation was terminated under § 139. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that as it read when the decree of divorce was entered, § 139 constituted a statutory reservation of the power of modification, including termination, of the provisions for future alimony installments in all decrees of divorce entered in the courts of California. The amendment to § 139 operated prospectively from the date of remarriage only upon installments of alimony not yet accrued at that time. It therefore could not have been said to deprive the wife of any right that had already vested in her by virtue of the decree.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
