Price v. Schwafel


Civ. No. 13956


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


92 Cal. App. 2d 77; 206 P.2d 683; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1650



May 26, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 21, 1949. Carter, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. John D. Foley, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel issuance of a building permit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which denied their request to compel defendant building inspector to issue a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The landowners sought a writ of mandamus to compel the issuance of a building permit for construction of a business. The landowners contended that an ordinance limiting the use of the landowners' property to residential purposes, as applied to the landowners, was arbitrary, unconstitutional, discriminatory, and confiscatory and not a proper exercise of the police power. The landowners also claimed that defendant city was estopped from setting up the ordinance as a defense in the action. The court found that the ordinance as applied to the landowners was valid. Zoning ordinances, or ordinances excluding any commercial use, had to be reasonable, and the use excluded had to bear some reasonable relation to the public interest. Where reasonable minds differed as to the propriety of the classification, the legislative determination was conclusive. Under the applicable principles, there could be but little doubt that the ordinance involved represented a valid exercise of the city's police power. The right to use private property could be restricted by an ordinance that followed a reasonable plan. Further, the evidence failed to show the essential elements of an estoppel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1897 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Ball


Civ. No. 16949


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


92 Cal. App. 2d 93; 206 P.2d 1111; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1653



May 26, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 10, 1949, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 21, 1949. Traynor, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County determining heirship. Stanley N. Barnes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an intestate's heirs at law, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that respondents, the relatives of the intestate's predeceased wife, were statutory heirs of the intestate and entitled to a undivided one-half interest in the intestate's personal property.


OVERVIEW: While living single in Pennsylvania, the intestate borrowed money to purchase certain stock. After marrying, the intestate and his wife moved to California. The stock-related debt was repaid entirely from the intestate's post-marriage earnings. Neither the intestate nor his predeceased wife left a will. The wife's relatives filed a petition for determination of heirship and claimed that under Cal. Prob. Code §§ 228, 229, they were entitled to all of the wife's separate property and one-half of the couple's community property. The intestate's heirs at law claimed that the entire estate was the intestate's separate property. The trial court found that the relatives were entitled to one-half of the intestate's personal property and that the heirs at law were entitled to the other one-half, together with all of the intestate's real property. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly reclassified the property acquired in Pennsylvania in accordance with California's community property laws. Because the stock was paid for after the marriage and the remaining personal property was acquired after the marriage, the relatives were statutory heirs under §§ 228, 229.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1898 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


French Art Cleaners v. State Board of Dry Cleaners


Civ. No. 13913


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


91 Cal. App. 2d 890; 206 P.2d 25; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1321



May 19, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 14, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County granting a preliminary injunction. Frank M. Ogden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State Board of Dry Cleaner, challenged an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) granting a preliminary injunction. The injunction enjoined the Board from enforcing as to respondent dry cleaner or seeking to enforce any of the price orders and price lists, and from establishing any minimum price schedules pursuant to the provisions of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 9553-9566 until further order of the trial court.


OVERVIEW: A majority of the Board's licensees in the county, pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 9563, filed a petition to establish minimum price schedules for various items of cleaning, dyeing, and pressing service. The dry cleaner alleged that the prices established by the Board were exorbitant and unfair to the public. It argued that if the minimum price schedules were enforced it would lose the lower price-bracket group of its customers. Simply because the injunction issued, the court noted that it did not necessarily follow that the trial court entertained the conviction that the legislation was unconstitutional. It could also be reasonably assumed that the trial court concluded that the Board would suffer no serious detriment by permitting prices to remain as they were, and that less harm would come by granting the injunction than by denying it. The court lastly noted that the Board's treatment of the case bore out the dry cleaner's contention that the facts relating to the actual conduct, practices, and usages of the trade, of which courts had no judicial knowledge, was required to be brought out at a trial, before any court could decide the ultimate question of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order and affirmed the order as modified.

 

1899 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Israel


Crim. No. 801


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


91 Cal. App. 2d 773; 206 P.2d 62; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1300



May 11, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 9, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County and from an order denying a new trial. Dan F. Conway, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery, grand theft, and possession of firearms by persons who had been convicted of felonies.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which convicted them of robbery, grand theft of automobiles, and violation of 1923 Cal. Stat. p. 695; Cal. Gen. Laws Act 1970, § 2 (1923) (as amended) for possession of firearms as persons who had been convicted of felonies. They also sought review of the order denying their motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with armed robbery of a used car lot office and grand theft of two automobiles. Each defendant had prior felonies and was found to be an habitual criminal under the Habitual Criminal Act, Cal. Penal Code § 644. On review, the court held that the evidence was amply sufficient to support the verdicts, including the positive identification of defendants by three witnesses, their possession of the second car, and their unsatisfactory explanations of that fact. By pleading not guilty to the counts charging possession of a prohibited firearm with a prior felony conviction, defendants put into issue all of the facts necessary for a conviction of the charge and thus the necessary reference to prior convictions could not be held to be prejudicial. Moreover, the trial court instructed the jury that, aside from purposes of impeachment, the evidence of the prior felony convictions could be considered only in reaching the verdicts on those possession counts. The court rejected defendants' contention that § 644 made the act of being a habitual criminal a separate felony, holding that the allegations of previous convictions were not allegations of substantive crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and the denial of their motion.

 

1900 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Citizens' Committee for Old Age Pensions v. Board of Supervisors


Civ. No. 16827


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


91 Cal. App. 2d 658; 205 P.2d 761; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1280



May 4, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 27, 1949. Carter, J., and Traynor, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders sustaining demurrers, granting motion to dismiss, granting motion to strike, and denying motion to file second amended complaint. Vernon W. Hunt, Judge pro tem.

Action for an injunction and for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed. Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed his action against defendants, Board of Supervisors of Los Angeles County and the County Supervisors Association. Plaintiff had sought an injunction to restrain an appropriation of funds by the board and a declaratory judgment stating that the appropriation was illegal and unauthorized.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer alleged that the statutes under which the board appropriated funds for the association were unconstitutional. At the hearing to show cause why the taxpayer's motion for a preliminary hearing should not be granted, it was learned that the board had already appropriated the funds and delivered them to the association. Thus, the issue of a preliminary injunction was moot. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the taxpayer's complaint, holding that because the injunctive relief was moot, only the declaratory relief was before the trial court. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to issue a declaratory judgment because it had discretion to do so if it determined that the declaratory judgment was not necessary or proper at the time. Secondly, the court held that it was not error for the trial court to refuse to permit the taxpayer to amend his first amended complaint at the hearing on the demurrers filed by the board and association. The taxpayer had not served the opposing parties with the proposed amendment or demonstrated why its filing was necessary or proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.The purported appeals from the trial court's orders were dismissed.

 

1901 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Heimann v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 16616


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


91 Cal. App. 2d 311; 204 P.2d 955; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1222



April 18, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 16, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County taxing costs on appeal. Stanley N. Barnes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an eminent domain proceeding, appellant landowners sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, upon motion by respondent condemnor, taxed the landowners' costs on appeal for printing briefs at $ 100 pursuant to Cal. R. App. 26(c).


OVERVIEW: The landowners obtained a judgment in their favor in an eminent domain action. The landowners filed their bill for costs, which included items aggregating $ 268.98 for printing briefs and other documents. Upon the condemnor's motion, the trial court taxed the landowners' costs for such printing at $ 100 pursuant to Rule 26(c). On appeal, the landowners' relied on a prior appellate opinion regarding costs. The order was affirmed. The court noted that there was no question in the prior appeal as to whether the amounts or the subject matter of the items of costs were proper. The court ruled that not all costs incurred by the landowners were recoverable. The landowners had to rely on a statute for an award of costs, and the measure of the statute was the measure of the right to recover costs. The court concluded that Rule 26(c) was a reasonable regulation in the matter of allowing costs for printing briefs, including the briefs in an eminent domain case. The trial court ruled correctly in striking out the amount of claimed costs for printing briefs in excess of $ 100. Under Rule 26(c), it was not discretionary with the trial court to allow more than $ 100 for printing briefs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1902 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Applegate


Crim. No. 718


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


91 Cal. App. 2d 163; 204 P.2d 689; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1199



April 7, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 5, 1949. Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County and from an order denying a new trial. L. N. Turrentine, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) for grand theft, in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 484, 951, 952, and the trial court's denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW:  Cal. Penal Code § 506 provided that every trustee who was entrusted with the control of property for the use of another person who fraudulently appropriated it to any use other than for what it was received was guilty of embezzlement. Here, defendant held money as the trustee and was obligated to turn the money over when demand was made for it. Defendant refused on the ground that the officers were squandering the money and that he had a claim against the association in excess of the amount demanded. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court reasoned that defendant's paying to the association of bad checks was evidence that the money was the property of the association. There was evidence from which the jury could conclude that the association had a legally recognizable interest in the money to support the embezzlement charge. Cal. Penal Code §§ 506, 506(a) was not unconstitutional when it was set out in clear and understandable language that was sufficient to enable persons of ordinary intelligence to determine the specific conduct that was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for grand theft.

 

1903 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Los Angeles v. Tower


Civ. No. 16466


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


90 Cal. App. 2d 869; 204 P.2d 395; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1065



March 30, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Thurmond Clarke, Judge.

Action to condemn land for right of way for a transmission line.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which awarded it compensation for a right of way for a high power transmission line condemned by respondent city and its department, over a corner of a triangular parcel of land containing approximately 138 acres.


OVERVIEW: The parcel taken consisted of about not quite two acres. The landowner contended that that amount awarded in its favor was insufficient. On appeal the landowner argued that the value of the property should have been fixed as of the date that the city went into physical possession of the property and not as of the date that the summons was issued. The court noted that in receiving evidence of value as of the date of trial and rejecting evidence of value as of the date when possession was taken the trial court was following the procedure outlined in Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1249. The landowner argued that § 1249 was inapplicable. The court disagreed and held that the statute applied. There was no conflict between § 1249 and Cal. Const. art. I, § 14. The court also determined that the landowner was afforded all of its constitutional rights with regard to the taking. The basis protection given by the constitution was that the owner could not have been divested of his title until full compensation was paid and the court concluded that the landowner was fully paid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1904 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Remmer v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 13926


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


90 Cal. App. 2d 854; 204 P.2d 92; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1062



March 29, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 28, 1949, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 26, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Edward P. Murphy, Judge.

Proceeding for a writ of prohibition to restrain further proceedings in an action, and an action for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments denying both the writ and the injunction, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, arrested individuals and a club, sought review of two decisions of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied the petition for a writ of prohibition and an injunction to restrain the trials of the individuals who had been arrested in raids of the club for keeping and maintaining a place where draw poker was carried on and conducted in violation of San Francisco, Cal., Police Code § 288.


OVERVIEW: The writ of prohibition sought to restrain the trial and the injunction sought to prevent further raids and arrests on similar charges. After the trial court denied the requests the individuals and the club filed two appeals, which were consolidated for review. The individuals and the club argued that § 288 was unconstitutional on the grounds that it was a duplication of state law and in conflict with that law, the portions that did not conflict with state law were inseparable from those that were in conflict and therefore the whole section must fall, and the legislation was unreasonable. The argument was that § 288 conflicted with Cal. Penal Code § 330. The court disagreed and determined that there was not a conflict that required invalidation of the ordinance. Neither draw, nor draw low ball poker was prohibited by state law and therefore San Francisco, Cal., Police Code § 288, when invoked against places where those gambling gamers were played, was not in conflict with Cal. Penal Code § 330, or any other state law. Finally, the court concluded that the legislation was not unreasonable or oppressive. The municipality had the right to condemn gambling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Estate of Gestner


Civ. No. 13949


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


90 Cal. App. 2d 680; 204 P.2d 77; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1034



March 18, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 16, 1949. Shenk, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco approving an account of a guardian of an incompetent's estate, overruling objections to the account, and refusing to direct payments for care and maintenance of the incompetent at a state hospital. T. I. Fitzpatrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, state department of mental hygiene (department), appealed an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which refused to direct respondent guardian to pay the department for the incompetent's board, care, and maintenance at a state hospital.


OVERVIEW: An incompetent was found insane at the time of the commission of a burglary and committed to a state hospital for the criminally insane. The probate court denied the department's petition for an order directing the guardian of the estate to pay the incompetent's board, care, and maintenance at the hospital on the ground that the matter was better threshed out in a civil action. The department appealed. The court reversed because the election to proceed under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6655 was that of the department and not the probate court, which was required to accept jurisdiction over all the issues that could have been raised in a proceeding under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6658. The court held that the estate was liable for care furnished before and after the 1945 amendment to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6650, which clarified the existing law regarding liability for care for persons committed to custodial confinement under Cal. Penal Code § 1026. The court found that § 6650 was not inconsistent with the veterans' guardianship law and or unreasonable in requiring establishment of sanity by jury rather than a superintendent's certificate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and instructed the probate court to hear the department's petition for an order directing the guardian to pay the cost of the incompetent's care at a state hospital.

 

1908 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Pearson


Civ. No. 7516


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


90 Cal. App. 2d 436; 203 P.2d 52; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 994



March 2, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Yuba County decreeing partial distribution and from an order settling the first account of an executor. Warren Steel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment annulled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant devisee sought reversal of the judgments of the Superior Court of Yuba County (California), which decreed partial distribution and settled the first account of appellee executor. The trial court authorized the executor to deduct the amount of the inheritance tax due the state, as well as the pro rata share of the federal estate tax, from the real and personal property that the executor proposed to distribute to the devisee.


OVERVIEW: The will provided that the real property left to the devisee was to be free and clear of all liens of any kind and character and description, and if there were any such liens at the time of the testator's death, the same were to be paid before any other payment or distribution. On appeal, the court made a de novo interpretation of the will and concluded that the testator intended the devisee to receive the real property but not the personal property free and clear of all liens, including tax liens. The court noted that Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 13401 et seq., made the tax a lien on transferred property, directed the executor to collect the tax from the transferee, and provided for nondelivery until collection. The court also noted that Cal. Prob. Code § 970 directed the executor to prorate the federal estate tax among the various distributees unless otherwise directed by the will. The court ruled that § 970 did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that in determining the amount of state inheritance and federal estate taxes that the executor was authorized to deduct from the devisee's share, the value of the real property could not be considered.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the order of the trial court and remanded the matter to the trial court.

Wheeler v. Gregg


Civ. No. 16444


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


90 Cal. App. 2d 348; 203 P.2d 37; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 984



February 28, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 21, 1949, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 28, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred L. Bartlett, Judge.

Action for a judgment declaring void a variance permit granted one defendant by defendant city, and for injunctive and other relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners filed an action for a declaration that the grant of a conditional use permit by respondent city council under Los Angeles, Cal., Ordinance No. 90500, § 12.24, to respondent applicant was unconstitutional. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered judgment for the city council and the applicant. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city council granted the applicant's request for a conditional use permit under Los Angeles, Cal., Ordinance No. 90500, § 12.24, to excavate his property for the development of natural resources. The property owners appealed and asserted that the city council acted outside its authority when it granted the permit, the ordinance unlawfully delegated legislative power to the city council, the grant of the permit was an unconstitutional exercise of police power, the city council was estopped to impair the personal and property rights of the property owners, the planned excavation would constitute a nuisance, and there was no evidence to support the trial court's findings of facts. The court held that the evidence did not establish that the ordinance was unconstitutional or void, the permit did not amend or alter the ordinance, the evidence showed that the excavation constituted a reasonable and necessary method of operation, property owners had no vested right in the exercise of police power, the excavation would not result in any substantial injury to the property owners, and substantial evidence supported the findings of fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the city council and the applicant was affirmed.

1911 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Export Leaf Tobacco Co. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 16460


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


89 Cal. App. 2d 909; 202 P.2d 622; 1949 Cal. App. LEXIS 1172



February 4, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Arthur Crum, Judge.

Action to obtain refund of personal property tax paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In respondent tobacco exporter's action to obtain a refund of personal property tax that appellant county assessed against a shipment of tobacco, the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered a judgment for the exporter and ordered the county to refund the tax. The county appealed. It contended that the conclusion of law that the tax was illegally assessed was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: The Virginia tobacco exporter placed a quantity of tobacco on a steamship for shipment to Hong Kong. The ship put in at Los Angeles to take on additional cargo. Because of the declaration of war with Japan and orders of the United States Navy, the voyage was terminated at Los Angeles. The exporter immediately made plans to ship the cargo by rail back to Virginia. The county taxed the cargo. In upholding the illegality of the tax, the court held that the tobacco was in the course of a foreign and interstate movement and in transit on the taxing date, and that it was not legally assessable or taxable by the county by virtue of the provisions of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. cl. 3, and the Export-Import Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 2. The court found that (1) the interruption in the shipment of the tobacco was an involuntary interruption caused by the intervention of duly constituted governmental authority owing to wartime conditions, and (2) the delay in Los Angeles did not constitute such a break in its foreign or interstate transit as to remove the tobacco from the protections of the Commerce Clause or the Export-Import Clause.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment that ordered the county to refund the personal property tax it assessed against the tobacco exporter was affirmed.

Rombotis v. Fink

Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One

Action to quiet title to real property and for declaratory relief, to which defendant filed a cross-complaint for foreclosure of a street improvement bond.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of appellee lien holder in the property owner's action to quiet title and for declaratory relief. The lien holder cross filed for payment.


OVERVIEW: The property in question had been assessed with delinquent taxes and was eventually owned by the state. The court reversed the prior ruling and found in favor of the property owner.

1915 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Sahlender


Civ. No. 13698


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


89 Cal. App. 2d 329; 201 P.2d 69; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1041



December 27, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 25, 1949. Carter, J., and Traynor, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco decreeing distribution of an estate. T. I. Fitzpatrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the remaindermen of a testamentary trust, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California). The judgment held that the trust was void in toto because several of its provisions violated the rule against perpetuities and the rule against restraints on alienation, and it awarded the entire estate to respondent, the testator's daughter.


OVERVIEW: The testator's testamentary trust gave its income to his daughter for life. If the daughter survived the testator but died within 24 years of the testator, and left issue, the child or children received the income until the 24-year period elapsed, at which time the trust terminated and the remainder interests vested in possession. The probate court found that the trust violated the rules against perpetuities and against restraints on alienation, that the invalid provisions were not severable from the trust, and that the daughter was entitled to the entire estate. The remaindermen argued that the rule against perpetuities did not exist in the State, and that even if it did, the invalid provisions were severable from the valid provisions. In reversing the probate court's judgment, the court held that the State had both the rule against restraints on alienation, with its statutory period of lives in being or 25 years, and the rule against remoteness of vesting, with its common-law period of lives in being and 21 years. The court found that several trust provisions violated the rule against perpetuities but that they were severable from the remainder of the trust.


OUTCOME: The judgment that held that the testamentary trust was invalid in toto because several of its provisions violated the rule against perpetuities and the rule against restraints on alienation, and which awarded the entire estate to the testator's daughter, was reversed.

 

1916 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


San Diego E. R. Co. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 7509


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


89 Cal. App. 2d 267; 200 P.2d 573; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1029



December 21, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 17, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Peter J. Shields, Judge.

Action to recover transportation license taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant transportation company sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which found in favor of respondent California Board of Equalization in its action against the Board to recover transportation license taxes it paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the transportation company argued that the trial court erred in denying its request for the recovery of transportation license taxes it paid the Board under protest. Upon review, the court found the transportation company's argument without merit. If the legislature intended, by the slight changes made in the wording of the law, that in determining gross receipts subject to taxation, only that portion of a single fare attributable to transportation in unincorporated territory should be taxed, no reason appeared why cryptic language should have been used. Where prorationing was intended, as provided in Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 9606, the legislature so provided in definite terms. Its failure to provide for the apportionment of gross receipts from intercity travel on a mileage basis, when it specifically so provided regarding interstate travel, was convincing evidence that no such result was intended. The fact that the legislature did not intend to provide for prorationing as claimed was indicated by Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 9652.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1917 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Welsh


Civ. No. 3723


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


89 Cal. App. 2d 43; 200 P.2d 139; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 995



December 6, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 4, 1949, and Petitioners and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 3, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of Fresno County denying petition by executors for ratable distribution insofar as it charged debts in manner "other than as herein set forth," directing that liens and expenses of administration other than those against specific property be charged against the residuary estate, directing that income and federal estate taxes be charged against specific bequests, and directing executors to recompute ratable distribution accordingly. Arthur C. Shepard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the executors of an estate and others, appealed orders of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), denying their petition for ratable distribution insofar as it charged debts in an estate dispute.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellants petition for ratable distribution insofar as it charged debts in a manner other than as set out in a will, which directed that liens and expenses of administration other than those against specific property be charged against the residuary estate and that income and federal estate taxes be charged against specific bequests. The executors were to recompute ratable distribution accordingly. The trial court found that the petition for ratable distribution, as supplemented, was contrary to the terms of the will and the law applicable, and did not correctly set forth the items chargeable against the gifts contained in the will and accordingly did not represent the net amount due to respondents, the legatees and devisees, after deduction of charges. The court found that the conclusion reached by the trial court was properly not in accord with appellants' contention that all of the burdens of the entire estate were to be charged ratably against all of the other bequests contained in the will. Section 822b of the Internal Revenue Code, 26 U.S.C.S. § 155, provided that the executors were to pay the federal estate tax.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1918 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Steiner v. Darby


Civ. Nos. 16587, 16588


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


88 Cal. App. 2d 481; 199 P.2d 429; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1490



November 12, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 10, 1949. Carter, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders sustaining demurrers to amended complaints. Clarence M. Hanson, Judge.

Actions for injunctive relief. Judgments of dismissal on sustaining demurrers to amended complaints without leave to amend.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county employees appealed judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) dismissing their actions for injunctive relief against defendant, the County of Los Angeles (county), and sustaining the county's demurrers to the county employees' complaints without leave to amend.


OVERVIEW: The county required its employees to take an oath of allegiance and to sign an affidavit avowing that during their employment with the county, they would not advocate the overthrow of the government by force and violence or become a member of an organization or political party advocating the same. The county employees sought an injunction to prevent the county from requiring them to execute the affidavit, alleging that the affidavit violated the federal and state constitutions. The trial court sustained the county's demurrers. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that in their position as civil servants, the county employees surrendered certain natural rights. Because the county employees did not have a constitutional right to their employment, the county could require them to forego their constitutional rights and privileges to the extent that the exercise of those rights and privileges would be inconsistent with the performance of their duties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court, dismissing the county employees' action for injunctive relief, and dismissed the appeals from the orders of the trial court sustaining the county's demurrers.

 

1919 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Fairchild v. Brock


Civ. Nos. 3813, 3814


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


88 Cal. App. 2d 425; 199 P.2d 9; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1485



November 10, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 3, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Orange County. Franklin G. West, Judge.

Actions for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants after orders sustaining demurrers to complaints without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff farmers sought review of two decisions of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which entered judgment in favor of defendant government officials in the farmers' actions that sought injunctive relief to prevent the officials from arresting the farmers for slaughtering animals.


OVERVIEW: The farmers each sought to have an animal slaughtered on his own farm. Neither farmer had a license to slaughter the animals and hired an individual to do the actual slaughtering. The officials contended that the farmers were engaged in or proposed to engaged in the business of slaughtering without a license as required by Cal. Agric. Code § 346 and did not fall within any exception to the license requirement. The court held that the farmers were exempt under Cal. Agric. Code § 356. However, the court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing the actions. The general rule was that an injunction would not be granted to protect a person from prosecution for the commission of a criminal offense. The farmers failed to assert that the statutes in question were unconstitutional and the court determined that they failed to plead facts sufficient to entitle them to injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

 

1920 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Franklin v. Peterson


Civ. No. 16329


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


87 Cal. App. 2d 727; 197 P.2d 788; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1385



September 28, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 22, 1948. Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Hartley Shaw and Jess E. Stephens, Judges.

Action for declaration of invalidity of an ordinance imposing a gross receipts tax.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) upholding the validity of Los Angeles, Cal., Code § 21.190 (1946) imposing a business license tax on the conduct of certain businesses within the city, in an action against respondents, city clerk and others. The attorney asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and that the city lacked authority to impose the tax.


OVERVIEW: The attorney brought a declaratory relief action against respondents attacking the constitutionality of § 21.190 on the grounds of vagueness and lack of authority in the city to impose a tax on occupations. The trial court rendered judgment for respondents, upholding the constitutionality of the ordinance, and the attorney appealed. The court affirmed, ruling that, although the ordinance had not specifically stated that it applied only to persons engaged in business within the city limits, it was manifest that it did. The court applied the rule that where an ordinance was susceptible of two constructions, the court would adopt the construction that rendered it valid and constitutional. The court further held that the contention that respondent city was without power to levy a business tax for revenue purposes was without merit. The city of Los Angeles had taken advantage of the privilege of legislative autonomy extended by the provisions of Cal. Const. art. XI, §§ 6, 8. The imposition of the tax for revenue purposes was a municipal affair, which the municipality possessed, and the city's charter had not limited that power. Thus, the court concluded that the tax was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for respondents in the attorney's action challenging the constitutionality and validity of a city ordinance imposing a tax on conducting business within the city.

1922 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reingold


Crim. No. 4213


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


87 Cal. App. 2d 382; 197 P.2d 175; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1341



September 2, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 30, 1948. Shenk, J., Edmonds, J., and Spence, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, from an order denying a new trial, and from verdicts. Charles W. Fricke, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order reversed with directions; appeal from verdicts dismissed. Judgment of conviction of first degree robbery, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which, by a jury verdict, convicted defendant of the crime of robbery. Defendant challenged the verdict and the trial court's denial of his motion for a new trial on the ground that there was insufficient evidence for the conviction because the accomplice's testimony was not corroborated as required by Cal. Penal Code § 1111.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion to quash and set aside the indictment, a motion that the court, of its own motion, dismiss the indictment under Cal. Penal Code § 1385, a demurrer to the indictment, and a motion for a separate trial. The motions were denied and the demurrer overruled. A jury found defendant guilty of robbery and the trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant contended that the verdict was contrary to the law and the evidence. A co-defendant implicated defendant in the robbery but defendant asserted that his testimony was not sufficiently corroborated as required by Cal. Penal Code § 1111. The court reversed defendant's conviction for robbery and the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial because the corroboration evidence for the accomplice's testimony was not sufficient to support defendant's conviction. The court concluded that the corroboration evidence presented failed to rise above a mere suspicion of guilt and did not sufficiently link defendant to the specific crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for robbery and the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

1923 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Elbert, Ltd. v. Nolan


Civ. No. 16108


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


87 Cal. App. 2d 24; 196 P.2d 88; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1288



July 30, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ruben S. Schmidt, Judge.

Action to quiet title to real property.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment for respondent tax sale purchaser in an action to quiet title to real property.


OVERVIEW: Certain property was assessed for taxation in 1932. When the taxes went unpaid, the tax collector sold the property to the state on September 2, 1933. The property was not redeemed and was deeded to the state on July 2, 1933. In 1945, the tax sale purchaser bought the property from the state. The tax sale purchaser brought an action to quiet title after the landowners claimed an interest in the property. The trial court quieted the title in favor of the tax sale purchaser. The landowners sought review and the court affirmed. The court rejected the landowners' claim that the deed to the state was improper because it was issued less than five years after the sale. The court agreed that under Cal. Pol. Code § 3785, it appeared that a deed made less than five years after the sale was invalid. However, the court said that that section was required to be read in concert with other sections of the Political Code pertaining to sales of delinquent tax property. Those sections originally set the time for the 1933 sale as July 1, but then extended the period by 61 days. Further, the court said, if no extension had been made, then the time for the sale would have been July 2, 1938.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment for a tax sale owner in an action to quiet title to real property claimed by the landowners.

 

1924 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Redwood Theatres, Inc. v. Modesto


Civ. No. 7450


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 2d 907; 196 P.2d 119; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1708



July 27, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Ralph McGee, Judge.

Action to restrain enforcement of a city ordinance imposing a license tax.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants on sustaining demurrers to complaint and amendments thereto without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff theater corporation (theater) appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California) that was entered in favor of defendants, city and city officers, in an action to enjoin the enforcement of a city license tax ordinance.


OVERVIEW: A theater challenged the trial court judgment entered in favor of the city and city officers in the theater's action to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance imposing a theater admission license tax. The theater claimed that the license tax constituted an impermissible double tax under Cal. Const. art. XIII and was imposed in a discriminatory manner. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the license did not constitute a double tax because art XIII applied to property and was inapplicable when a municipality imposed a license for the purpose of regulation of revenue. The court observed that the mere fact that a business was required to pay regulatory taxes under the police power and also pay additional property taxes for the purpose of revenue under another ordinance did not render the ordinances void on the grounds of double taxation which did not apply to excises. The court explained that the city ordinance was an authorized levy and collection of license taxes for conducting business within the city. The court further found absent a city charter provision prohibiting such a levy, the license tax was a substantive and procedurally valid exercise of municipal police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment sustaining the imposition and enforcement of a theater admission license tax ordinance against the theater corporation by the city and the city officers.

 

1925 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Birch Sec. Co.


Civ. No. 7444


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


86 Cal. App. 2d 703; 196 P.2d 143; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1672



July 12, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 7, 1948, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 8, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Malcolm C. Glenn, Judge.

Action to recover corporate franchise tax.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff, the State of California, in its action to recover corporate franchise taxes from defendant corporation pursuant to the provisions of the Bank and Corporation Franchise Tax Act, Stats. 1929, p. 19, and amends.; 3 Deering's Gen. Laws, p. 3010, Act 8488. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state filed suit against a corporation for franchise taxes due and payable for the years 1935 and 1936, pursuant to the provisions of the tax statute. The trial court found in favor of the state. The corporation appealed, contending that the tax did not apply to it as a foreign corporation and that the action was barred by res judicata. The court rejected both contentions, finding that evidence at trial supported the finding that the corporation was actively engaged in business transactions in California for financial and pecuniary profit and therefore liable for taxes. The court also found that a federal judgment was not res judicata of the issues of the suit. The court noted that the former federal judgment, which was offered in evidence as a bar to this action, was merely against certain named officers of the state, as such, and not against the State of California. The court therefore found that the federal case was not a suit against the State of California, and it was therefore not res judicata in the action or an estoppel against the state maintaining the action for unpaid franchise taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

1926 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Bodkin


Crim. No. 2528


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


86 Cal. App. 2d 208; 194 P.2d 588; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1606



June 15, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner instituted a proceeding against the State seeking a writ of habeas corpus to secure his release from custody. Petitioner was convicted of a violation of a city ordinance prohibiting the obstruction of a street or sidewalk by a crowd or persons when directed by police officers to disburse. Petitioner was standing on a lightly-traveled street addressing between 100 and 150 workers on the Taft-Hartley Act then pending before Congress.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was directed to move on by a police officer but refused to do so. The conviction was affirmed on appeal. Petitioner contended that the ordinance was unconstitutional in that it was an abridgment of the rights of free speech and assembly and was a violation of the privileges and immunities clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Petitioner particularly asserted that the United States Supreme Court, by case law dictum, limited the scope of regulations on the user of streets for public meetings to "busy" streets or intersections. The court disagreed and held that the essence of the issue was whether or not the regulation was reasonable. The court held that the ordinance was constitutional and did not prevent, or attempt to prevent, any use of the public streets which did not obstruct the free passage of the general public; rather, it prohibited the obstruction of passage of some members of the public along the street. Whether the obstruction merely impaired the progress of one member of the general public, or a thousand, did not alter the case and the factual determination that petitioner obstructed the passage of persons and refused to leave when requested.


OUTCOME: The writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1927 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Morgan


Crim. No. 4248


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


86 Cal. App. 2d 217; 194 P.2d 800; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1608



June 15, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to prevent extradition under Uniform Criminal Extradition Act.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner brought a proceeding in habeas corpus to prevent extradition under the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Cal. Penal Code § 1549.1.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with conspiring to aid in the commission of the crime of grand larceny. A warrant was issued for his arrest for the purpose of his extradition to Colorado. He was placed under arrest and detained in Los Angeles. Petitioner contended that his arrest and detention were unlawful in that Cal. Penal Code § 1549.1 was in conflict with the Constitution and laws of the United States. Petitioner was not in Colorado on the date that the alleged crime was committed. Thus, he argued that he could not have fled or been a fugitive from justice as stated in U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 2 or 18 U.S.C.S. § 662. Under Cal. Penal Code § 1549.1 there was no requirement that in an extradition proceeding the accused must have fled from justice. Petitioner argued that this was inconsistent with 18 U.S.C.S. § 662 because the demanding state, Colorado, had not also adopted such a statute on extradition. The court held that § 662 placed minimum requirements on the duty to extradite and did not prevent or preempt the States from allowing extradition on lower standards. Secondly, reciprocity was not a requirement for extradition to the demanding state.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the writ of habeas corpus and remanded petitioner to custody.

 

1928 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Trans-Oceanic Oil Corp. v. Santa Barbara


Civ. No. 16227


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 2d 776; 194 P.2d 148; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 981



June 2, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 29, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. Ernest D. Wagner, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city and members of city council to annul their action in revoking a permit to drill an oil well, and to reinstate the permit.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which denied the corporation's writ of mandate to compel defendants, city, its mayor, and city council (council), to annul and rescind their action in revoking a permit for the drilling of an oil well within the city limit.


OVERVIEW: The corporation owned an oil lease for 10 years over approximately 80 acres in the city. The corporation applied to the council for a permit to drill an additional well. Santa Barbara, California Ordinance No. 1613, which governed the issuance of drilling permits, provided for a hearing by the council on each application and provided that a permit should be granted unless it materially affected the health and safety of the public. The council granted the corporation's permit, and the corporation promptly commenced drilling the well. A subsequently enacted city zoning ordinance prohibited oil drilling in the area of the city. The council revoked the corporation's permit at a special meeting without any notice and without a hearing. The trial court held that the revocation was a valid exercise of the city's police power. The court disagreed and held that the council could not exercise unlimited discretion to revoke permits. The corporation had a vested property right under the permit. The corporation had begun construction of the oil well and incurred liability for future work. The court held that the corporation's permit could not be revoked arbitrarily without cause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the city, its mayor, and council arbitrarily revoked the corporation's permit to drill an oil well without prior notice, without a hearing, without evidence, and in violation of the corporation's right to due process. The court ordered the trial court to grant the corporation's writ of mandate.

 

1929 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


County of Ventura v. Southern California Edison Co.


Civ. No. 15994


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 2d 529; 193 P.2d 512; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 946



May 18, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 15, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County. Charles F. Blackstock, Judge.

Action to recover expenses incurred by county and county fire protection district in fighting and extinguishing a fire.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which rendered judgment in favor of respondents, county and fire protection district, in an action to recover expenses incurred by respondents in fighting and extinguishing a fire.


OVERVIEW: A power transmission line came into contact with a telephone line and telephone pole, thereby causing a fire in the grass beneath the lines which spread into and burned over a large area of adjoining ranchland. The corporation owned and operated both the power and telephone lines. Respondents brought an action to recover from the corporation the expenses incurred by their fighting and extinguishing the fire, under the fire liability law, 1931 Cal. Stat. 1644. The case was consolidated for purposes of trial with two other actions filed against the corporation by persons whose property was damaged by the same fire. Judgment was rendered in favor of all plaintiffs, but the corporation only appealed from the judgment in favor of respondents. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the corporation, charged with knowledge of the condition of its equipment, took no steps to prevent the occurrence of fire, which was the reasonably foreseeable consequence of that condition. The court held that the fire liability law treated all persons similarly situated in the same manner and that the classification made by the statute was a rational and justifiable one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that rendered its judgment in favor of respondents and against the corporation in an action brought by respondents to recover expenses incurred by them in fighting and extinguishing a fire.

 

1930 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. State


Civ. No. 16049


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


85 Cal. App. 2d 361; 193 P.2d 11; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 919



May 4, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Hartley Shaw, Edward T. Bishop and Jess E. Stephens, Judges.

Action for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants on sustaining demurrers to complaint without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff painter appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found for defendants, the State of California and various state and county officials (state), in an action by the painter to restrain the state from prosecuting the painter for violations of the California Business and Professions Code by reason of his entering into contracts as a painter for considerations other than wages.


OVERVIEW: The painter instituted an action against the state to challenge the requirement that the painter possess a contractor's license and to restrain the state from prosecuting him for carrying on his business without a license. The superior court sustained the state's demurrers to the complaint without leave to amend and entered judgment for the state. The court affirmed and held that the licensing requirement applied to the business of painting buildings and other structures, that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7-26, the section defining contractors, was not void for uncertainty, and that the California Business and Professions Code was not unconstitutional. The court held that if all contractors were not builders under the common definitions of those words, then they were made so by the special definition of the statute and that a painting contractor was a contractor under the statutory definition. The court also found that the regulation of the business of painting contractors was within the state's police powers and served the public interest by providing protection against possible frauds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment, which was entered in favor of the state, and sustained without leave to amend the demurrers to the painter's complaint that sought to restrain the state from prosecuting the painter for violations of the California Business and Professions Code.

People v. Foogert


Crim. No. 2056


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


85 Cal. App. 2d 290; 193 P.2d 14; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 909



April 30, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 27, 1948. Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County and from an order denying a new trial. George F. Buck, Judge pro tem.

Prosecution for concealment of stolen goods.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California), which entered a judgment of conviction against him after a jury found him guilty of concealment of stolen goods, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 496bb, and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of concealing a vehicle that was stolen in another county, painted, and stored in a garage in the county where he was charged. After the trial court denied his request for a new trial, defendant appealed. On appeal, defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support the judgement because, first, even if he had committed the crime as charged, it occurred more than three years before the indictment. Therefore, the statute of limitations had run. Second, the crime, if committed by defendant, was committed in another jurisdiction. On review, the court held that the evidence showed specific affirmative acts of concealment calculated to conceal the car from its owner at the time charged in the indictment and not merely one act of concealment. The court further held that there was ample evidence that the car's storage in a camouflaged state, the failure to register the vehicle, among other things, were all acts of concealment within the county of jurisdiction. Finally, the court noted that the verdict was proper in that it expressed an intent to convict for the crime charged, and the form of the verdict was not material.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1932 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Downing v. California State Board of Pharmacy


Civ. No. 13680


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


85 Cal. App. 2d 30; 192 P.2d 39; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 868



April 15, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco granting a preliminary injunction. Thomas M. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state authorities sought review of an order from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted a preliminary injunction restraining them from arresting, prosecuting, or interfering with plaintiff drug manufacturers from making or supplying their drug in the manufacturers' suit for injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturers were arrested for conspiracy to violate Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26280 and Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26286. They filed a suit for injunctive relief against the state authorities and the trial court granted a preliminary injunction restraining them from arresting, prosecuting, or interfering with the manufacturers from making or supplying their drug. Upon review, the court reversed the order and discharged the preliminary injunction. The court held that the manufacturers were making and supplying a drug as defined by Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26200 because it was being used for medicinal purposes as a pain reliever. The court held that the manufacturers, in their complaint for the injunction, failed to show compliance with the provisions of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 26288, and thus they were not entitled to the preliminary injunction. The court held that the trial court had no power to permit even a limited violation of criminal statutes; thus, because the preliminary injunction permitted and authorized a limited violation of the statutes, its grant was error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of a preliminary injunction against the state authorities restraining them from arresting, prosecuting, or interfering with the manufacturers from making or supplying their drug in the manufacturers' suit for injunctive relief.

1934 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Wolff


Civ. No. 13556


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


84 Cal. App. 2d 435; 190 P.2d 665; 1948 Cal. App. LEXIS 1216



March 19, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 17, 1948. Shenk, J., and Schauer, J., Voted for a Hearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Pat R. Parker, Judge assigned.

Proceeding in mandamus, for an injunction and for declaratory relief with respect to rates of pay for certain municipal employees.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for petitioners affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and county, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in favor of plaintiff municipal employees with respect to a proceeding in mandate for an injunction and declaratory relief concerning their right to receive rates of pay identical to those received by private employees pursuant to collective bargaining agreements with private employers.


OVERVIEW: The municipal employees sought injunctive and declarative relief contending that under City and County of San Francisco, Calif., Charter § 151 they were entitled to receive rates of pay identical to those received by private employees pursuant to collective bargaining agreements with private employers. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the municipal employees. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of § 151 and allowed the municipal employees the claimed rates of pay. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court ruled that §151 was not an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The court determined that § 151 did not violate Cal. Const. art. XI, § 13 because § 13 did not regulate what could be done by a municipal corporation by charter provision. The court ruled that the enumeration of powers in Cal. Const. art. XI, § 8 1/2 did not act as an exclusion of any powers not listed. The court determined that the mandate of City and County of San Francisco, Calif., Charter § 151 that the take-home pay of public employees should be the same as private employees obviously included holiday pay and premium pay for night work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the municipal employees with respect to the proceeding in mandate for an injunction and declaratory relief concerning their entitlement to receive rates of pay identical to those received by private employees pursuant to collective bargaining agreements with private employers.

 

1935 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Spalliero


Crim. A. No. 13113


Appellate Department, Superior Court of California, Los Angeles


54 Cal. App. 3d Supp. 1; 126 Cal. Rptr. 469; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1658



November 20, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. 31490496, Bonnie Lee Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, entered by the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), for possession of a motor vehicle master key in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 466.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 466.5(a), in that he willfully, unlawfully, and with intent to use it in the commission of an unlawful act, possessed a motor vehicle master key. Defendant argued that the statute was too vague to meet due process requirements. The trial court convicted defendant and he appealed. On appeal the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that as long as a key operated more than one lock or ignition switch, but each such lock or ignition switch also could be operated by a key that would not work in the lock or ignition switch of any other vehicle whose lock or switch could be operated by the first key, then the first key was a master key. Defendant also argued that the statute was vague and uncertain because it referred, in the singular, to a key, while the evidence at the trial showed that more than one key was necessary to constitute a set capable of opening all of the cars of a given group. The court concluded that the argument overlooked the fact that Cal. Penal Code § 7 stated that the singular number included the plural.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possessing a motor vehicle master key because the statute was not fatally vague and gave defendant fair warning of the proscribed conduct.

 

1936 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lockheed Shipbuilding & Constr. Co.


Crim. A. No. 13179


Appellate Department, Superior Court of California, Los Angeles


50 Cal. App. 3d Supp. 15; 123 Cal. Rptr. 778; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1832



August 1, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. 413019, George W. Trammel III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, company and two employees, sought review of various convictions on several counts of misdemeanor violations of safety provisions of the labor code by the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California). The trial court convicted appellants for failing to follow special orders given by the engineer with the California Division of Industrial Safety.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, company and two employees, were convicted of misdemeanor violations for failure to follow special orders by the California Division of Industrial Safety under Cal. Lab. Code §§ 6300- 6604. Counts were tried separately and as a result, some convictions were reviewed before the other counts were tried and it was found unconstitutional to predicate criminal charges on the orders issued under Cal. Lab. Code § 6313 because the statute provided no prior notice to appellants and no opportunity to be heard. The court reversed the convictions and found that the special orders appellants were convicted of violating were unconstitutional. The instructions given to the jury at trial purported to give the special orders the effect of law in violation of the requirement that safety orders be promulgated in compliance with due process prerequisites of notice and hearing, and therefore, the misdirection of the jury was not harmless error under Cal. Const. art. VI, § 13. Additionally, supervisors, such as two employee appellants, were excluded from Cal Lab. Code § 6304 by amendment in 1973.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the misdemeanor convictions based on the special orders because such convictions were deemed unconstitutional between the time appellants, company and two employees, were convicted on different counts. The court applied the standard that they were unconstitutional because the statute provided no prior notice to appellants of intent to issue them and no opportunity to be heard concerning their issuance.

People v. Singer


Crim. A. No. 13236


Appellate Department, Superior Court of California, Los Angeles


50 Cal. App. 3d Supp. 9; 123 Cal. Rptr. 460; 1975 Cal. App. LEXIS 1349



July 25, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, No. 804769, Lawrence Waddington, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vendor sought review of the order of the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of violating Los Angeles City Ord. No. 95789 § 2, subd. h and Cal. Penal Code § 602.4 for selling newspapers at the Los Angeles International Airport.


OVERVIEW: Appellant vendor sold alternative newspapers at the airport. He did not have a permit to sell newspapers, and one vendor was granted the exclusive permit to sell the newspapers, with the unilateral right to decide which ones were sold. Appellant was convicted of violating Los Angeles City Ord. No. 95789 § 2, subd. h and Cal. Penal Code § 602.4 both of which precluded commercial activity at the airport without a permit. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 602.4 did not apply and, as the prosecutor concurred, treated the concurrence as a reversal of the conviction under that charge. The court held that the ordinance was too broadly drawn and interfered with appellant's protected rights to free speech under U.S. Const. amend. 1, and further held that the city's action in giving the unilateral right to decide what newspapers were sold to the single vendor licensed to sell newspapers also violated U.S. Const. amend. 1. The court reversed the conviction and found that the sidewalks were a historical forum for free speech and the prohibitions against commercial activity at the airport were not balanced with the right to free speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions because the city ordinance and the manner in which the sole holder of the newspaper permit determined what newspapers were to be sold at the airport violated the First Amendment and because the prosecutor conceded that the penal code provision did not apply to the activities at the airport.
